Objectives: To widespread the project results and to engage stakeholders, while raising awareness and knowledge 
transfer about circular economy and innovations produced by A2C. Specifically : i) Design the dissemination and 
communication strategy to support the public engagement, the project sustainability and the widespread of results. 
ii) To widespread general knowledge about food and plastic waste and the circular economy concept. iii) To deliver 
a framework for autonomous learning and capacity bu ilding.  iv) To implement actions to reach an optimal D&C 
performance and to periodically assess their implementation and capacity for raising awareness & engagement. vi) 
To support all partners in communicating /disseminating their results and to enhance the transferability potential 
together with the WP7. It includes the support to the Public Engagement strategy and actions from WP7.
8.1 A2C Outreach Strategy. (M1- M4). Leader: ICONS.  
The Communication and Dissemination (C&D) Strategy (CDS) will include the stakeholder characterisation, 
mapping, definition of phases for disseminating the project, communication campaigns and thematic campaigns, 
tools, actions, channels, timing and geographical specifications in order to provide a strategy tail ored to each local 
community but also to the EU -wide context. It will include KPIs, evaluation checkpoints, timing and procedures.  
Continuous monitoring of KPIs and analysis of the effectiveness of the strategy and impacts from C&D activities 
will be conducted. C&D activities will be coordinated by the Outreach Manager (ICONS), while coordinating a 
Local Outreach Desk (PRIMA) in charge of tailor the CDS to the local context exploiting the most effective tools 
& channels, reach local/regional/national stakeholders and communities. The information and data collected and 
the knowledge gathered by A2C will be shared with the CCRI (T8.5).    
60
8.2 Project identity and online channels. (M1- M4). Leader: ICONS. Others: All 
Visual identity and online channels will be generated, and settled a well -defined brand identity and related 
communication material (website, social media channels,  flyer, roll-up, project presentation video, etc.), and the 
main online communication and engagement project’s channels. Other c ommunication materials will be produced 
to support local engagement. The A2C website  (M2: landing page, M4: launch)  will be constantly updated with 
information on the project’s activities . A specific session will be dedicated to the A2C cluster with conten ts 
developed in Spanish and managed by the Local Outreach desk. The website will host a stakeholder platform as a 
two-way communication tool. The management of the website contents will be backed up by a social media 
strategy. In addition, A2C project will launch a Twitter and LinkedIn account.
8.3 Communication and engagement at local and regional level. (M5- M36). Leader: PRIMA Others: PROEX, 
AGRO, KVC, ICONS, CARM, CJM, INFO. 
The Local Outreach desk will implement Social Communication campaigns designed for enhancing and aligning 
with the public and citizenship eng agement strategy (T7.1).  Specific actions  already proposed:  -PROEX: 
engagement plan targeting local/regional primary agricultural stakeholders  through specific actions and raising 
awareness. -AGRO will organize conferences/workshops targeting local/regional industrial sector, facilitating their 
circular economy approach and offering an administrative support desk facilitating their circular transition as well 
as promote issuing regional recognitions to the successful ones. General public will be also engaged through tailored 
organized events.-PRIMA will carry out local/regional awareness actions,  targeting also the young public : (1) 
lectures/workshops at regional schools, Universities and educative events to raise awareness on A2C topics (M9-
M20, twice/weekly). (2)Regional contests for scholars aimed to spread the circular economy approach and fostering 
their involvement in these practices. Students will dare to solve a problem related to the sustainability of a 
product/processing waste. Best solutions will receive a recognition at an organize d event. (3) Short documentary 
production involving several actors (Alhama de Murcia municipality, local companies, students), arising awareness 
about project topics and fostering community  engagement on circular and climate neutral practices. It will be 
submitted to film contests related to the topic. ( 4) A youngster videogame  production, based on the waste 
management of a product manufacturing process.  
Additionally, communication will focus o n local/regional dissemination of results  through content packaging 
and relations with key stakeholders, stimulating social acceptance and replication. Dedicated publications will 
be produced and some Public Deliverables will be edited in an easy reading mode.
8.4 Outreach at European level. (M1- M36). Leader: ICONS. Others: All 
Content packaging, supporting the dissemination of A2C results and the project’s exploitation strategy, include: a) 
biannual eNewsletter; b) dedicated info-packs in an easy-to-read format supported by visual tools (i.e. infographics/ 
factsheets), with specific A2C contents for each  target group c) abstracts of key Public Deliverables, edited to 
facilitate their dissemination d) project final publication: A2C Best Practices Book (electronic & printable format), 
includes guidelines, lessons learnt and recommendations e) scientific & technical publications. Public outreach: 
contents addressing the general public, including citizens and stakeholders at large, aimed at widespread distribution 
(through European and global information multipliers and media) include: a) press & news releases, to raise project 
topics visibility, challenges and results, promoting A2C events; b) independent journalistic articles around A2C 
and related topics; c) audiovisual productions : short video interviews with project experts, stakeholders’ 
representatives,  decision-makers, and a final video on the main outcomes d) dedicated social media campaigns at 
EU and international level on occasion of thematic World Days and other EU initiatives.
8.5 Networking and clustering activities. (M5- M36).  Leader: EURA. Others: All    
An intensive networking activity will be conducted by all partners. Specific activities will include: a) Mobilization 
of key European and international stakeholders and associations (industry, academia, consumer associations, NGOs) 
fostering the connection of A2C with international markets and players and with Circular Economy Action Plans, EU 
Bioeconomy Strategy and the European Industrial Strategy at local, regional, national, European and international 
levels b) B2B meetings, participation in external events, organization of project events at EU level (workshops and 
other dissemination events with EU stakeholders and decision -makers, the final event at EU level) at 
local/regional/country level. c) Clustering with existing relevant European projects and initiatives on the circula r 
economy and the circular bioeconomy d) Cooperation with other circular territorial clusters funded under this topic. 
Close collaboration with the CCRI will be sought to maximise impacts through all the specific activities and 
ensure a wider dissemination among a large number of stakeholders and policy-makers.
8.6 Training, knowledge transfer and guidelines/recommendations to promote A2C  circular model. (M9- 
M36).  Leader: UVEG. Others: PRIMA, AGRO, PROEX, KVC, ICONS, UB, EURA, CARM, INFO, TCA, LPK 
It will be elaborated specific resources and open learning materials to contribute to the promotion of the model, 
taking into account the facilitators and barriers identified in WP7. It will be designed and executed an autonomous 
but comprehensive training plan f or local actors and education services for local communities and training 
modules/guidelines for EU stakeholders to better implement/transfer the knowledge acquired during the project 
and all lessons learnt, contributing to both a more effective development of circular solutions and to foster the 
61 
 
communities’ environmental awareness and sustainable habits, business and co -creation. Among other s: a) 
business models for circular economy innovations; b) financing and regulatory issues related to CE. 
A set of guidelines for fostering public engagement in circular economy projects  will be also generated by 
conducting a joint reflection on the ways for fostering effecti ve communication & public engagement for circular 
economy projects and environmental community-based initiatives, contributing to the know-how and the literature 
at EU about participatory and co -creation frameworks applied to environmental fields. The elaboration of these 
guidelines will require the p articipation of stakeholders from the quadruple helix in workshops, focus groups and 
DELPHI studies.  
At regional level, PRIMA will also develop a n industry mentoring programme aimed at generating innovative 
results-oriented ideas to respond to circular business challenges, through A2C multidimensional approach.

8.7 Exploitation strategy and long-term feasibility (M5-M36). Leader: ICONS. Others: All partners 
8.7.1 Mapping of Key Exploitable Results: Identifies all projects’ results through an initial webinar, introducing 
exploitation concepts and helping partners identifying them. From inputs from all other work packages and direct 
interviews with A2C partners, a comprehensive mapping of exploitable results will be produced. The resulting 
library will provide the basis for a comprehensive deployment strategy focusing on different exploitation pathways. 
8.7.2 IPR Assessment: Analyses background and foreground associated to each result, reaching consensus among 
IP owners and assessing the proper IPR measures while timely addressing all the potential issues that may hamper 
A2C exploitation routes. If needed, it will established connections with the European IPR Helpdesk support services. 
8.7.3 Innovation monitoring and market analysis: It will focus on the evolving socio-economic context including 
user needs, overall market trends, stakeholders and competitors, with particular reference to the outputs susceptible 
to be exploited, as well as the general considerations applied to generat e new circular business at EU level. The 
analysis will be based on desk research and questionnaires to stakeholders.  8.7.4 Exploitation Plan (EP): Develops 
and updates an exploitation roadmap that will coordinate and document both the joint and the individual strat egies 
of the consortium after the project’s end. At the project level, the Exploitation plan will focus on: i) Clarifying further 
research areas/needs, ii) Assessing a ctivities and resources needed to reach higher TRLs, iii) Defining an overall 
governance to accelerate the move of research results to market, iv) Assessing partners’ role in driving the replication 
and upscaling of solutions after the end of the project (in coordination with WP7), v) Providing framework business 
plans of commercial solutions, based on the outcomes of WP6. At the partner level, the plan will report individual 
partners’ exploitation strategies to leverage results within their own organisatio ns. Two dedicated workshops 
involving all partners will be organized during the project progress meetings, involving all the partners to collect 
inputs for further exploitation analysis.
8.8 Standardization activities. (M1- M36). Leader: UNE. Others: all tech partners 
T8.8.1: Analysis of the applicable standardization landscape (M1-M5): Based on the activities and the needs of 
the WPs, the applicable existing standards and those under development will be identified. The availability of this 
information at an early stage in the project provides for its consideration and facilitates the compatibility of the 
project outcomes with current market practises. T8.8.2: Contribution to the ongoing and future standardization 
developments (M6-M36): A2C will interact with the relevant technical standardization committees. This will also 
allow capturing their inputs as stakeholders and using the standardization system as a fast and highly focussed 
dissemination tool to the market stakeholders. Building on this, A2C will contribute to new standards developments 
in specific topics related to the A2C objectives by providing information, participating in ongoing works, submitting 
technical proposals for the modification of existing standards or even promoting the elaboration o f new standard 
documents like technical specifications (TS). The development of fast track standards like CEN -Workshop 
Agreements (CWA) will be studied.

Objectives. To structure, foster and daily maintain a high level of commitment from all partners  and to provide

following up the fulfilment of the project’s goals, through periodical and detailed control of all tasks and potential

9.1. Project Coordination, Quality Assurance and Risk Management (M1-M36). Leader: CETEC. Other: All. 
This task sets the processes for the overall A2C project management, ensuring decision-making, clear an operational 
internal communication, just as metric and timely risk control. -Set up a quality assessment mechanism based on 
project metrics that will be introduced in D9.1, then elaborated as the project evolves, and periodically reported in 
the Periodic Reports. -Monitor the project, aided by all WP leaders, for foreseeable potential risks and promptly 
initiating contingency plans to lessen or eliminate t heir negative effects. -Establish a bottom -up and top -down 
communication flow among all the partners that will include decision -making not only in terms of discussion of 
internal milestones, risks and deliveries, but also in terms of external positioning, key alliances and sustainability of 
the project’s results.-Set up management structures featuring clear responsibilities for all relevant partners.-Establish 
& coordinate all the management processes including, but not limited to, transversal coordination of all partners and 
WPs according to the work plan and the project’s objectives, external reviews, internal meetings, compilation, 
circulation of meeting minutes and action points, reporting procedures & communication channels. 
9.2. Administrative and Financial Coordination (M1 to M36). Leader: CETEC. Others: All partners 
This task includes the daily management of all legal, financial and administrative issues; both within the consortium 
and also with regards to their formal communication to the EC:  -Monitors full compliance with the current 
regulations of all activities, agreements, amendments, expenditures, IPR management and any other relevant issue 
at stake. -Sets up a secure, organized and useful collaborative space for the efficient communication, coll aboration 
and exchange of documents among all partners (M3). Maintain and deliver templates for all the financial, 
administrative and reporting duties of all partners. -Ensures periodic reporting and communication with the EC for 
purposes of coordination, progress monitoring and reporting; including the preparation and submission of Periodic 
and final Reports (M18, M36). -Requests, collects and review inputs from all partners with regards to any report, 
official deliverable, document and/or information as required by the EC or by the own daily routine of the project. 
This will include an additional layer of internal reporting, in the form of internal Activity Reports (periodic technical 
reports plus an overall follow-up of the Use of Resources and expenses) due every six months -Implementing any 
potential change in the Grant Agreement by ensuring the fulfilment of the contractual obligations in the Grant 
Agreement such as, but not limited to, the provision of payments.  
Task 9.3 Ethical issues management and Data Protection issues (M1-36). Lead: UVEG. Others: All partners 
An Ethics Handbook will be developed and will contain ethical measures when conduct ing research with humans 
and monitoring mechanisms as well as ethics benchmarks. Moreover, this task will cover the assessment and follow-
up of relevant ethical issues related to the project in each stage of the project with the final goal of protecting th e 
rights, the security and welfare of the participants in the project. In addition, specific  attention will be paid to data 
management to monitor compliance with data protection issues by developing a data management plan. If required, 
this task will cover the preparat ion of documents - according to EU and national regulatory frameworks - to be 
submitted to et hics authorities prior to start of the participant’s involvement such as: informed co nsent forms, 
information sheets. 
 
Deliverables: D.9.1 Project Management Guideline & Quality Plan (Report-CO; CETEC, M3). D.9.2 Project 
reports. Non official reports of technical, financial and risk analysis (Report -CO; CETEC, M9, M27).  D.9.3 
Ethics Handbook (Report-CO; UVEG, M6). Guidelines to manage with all relevant ethical issues.  D.9.4 Data 
management plan (Report-CO;UVEG,M12). Description of the data management life cycle for the data collected, 
processed and/or generated along the project. The first version of the DMP will include an evaluation of the ethics 
risks related to the data processing activities of the project and an opinion if a DPIA should be performed.

3.2. MANAGEMENT STRUCTURES, MILESTONES AND PROCEDURES 
3.2.1. MANAGEMENT STRUCTURE 
The Agro2Circular management structure is illustrated in 
Figure 16. The consortium and management structure will 
promote an optimal use of the knowledge, experience and 
expertise of the partners in fulfilling the objectives of the 
project, while providing effective project monitoring and 
control.  
The consortium organisati onal structure will comprise the 
bodies shown in following Table 51. 
 
General 
Assembly (GA) Responsible for the strategic decisions and the ultimate decision -making body. The GA will consist of one representative of each consortium 
partner and will be chaired by the Coordinator’s representative. The General Assembly assisted by the Technical Committee and the Exploitation 
Committee will articulate the management of the project at the strategic level. The GA will meet at least twice a year. Any member party of the 
consortium should be represented at any meeting of such consortium body and may appoint a substitute to attend and vote at a ny meeting. Any 
decision may also be enforced if the Project Coordinator circulates it to all members of the consortium in written form and i t is then agreed upon 
by the majority of the consortium. The GA will be free to act on its own initiative to formulate proposals and take decisions in accordance with the 
set procedures. The following decisions will be taken by the GA: changes to the consortium configuration, major changes of the work plan, major 
budget shifts, reallocation of work, IPR issues settlement of problems differences between contractors or partners. 
Table 51. A2C consortium organisational structure  
Figure 16. Agro2Circular 
Management Structure 
64 
 
Technical 
Committee 
(TC) 
Coordinates technological issues. It follows the work done in work packages and ensures the coherence of implementation and t echnical work 
progress plus manages technical matters arising from the work undertaken in each WP. The TC consists of a maximum one delegate from each 
partner up to a maximum of five participants for the Committee. Initially the TC will be made up of CETEC, CTNC, KVC, ECO and GWC. The TC 
members may be renewed annually by voting in the GA. The decisions taking and voting procedures are described in the Consortium Agreement. 
The TC is also responsible for risk management, quality assurance and the technological and scientific progress assessment of all project outputs 
that are delivered to the European Commission, including the accomplishment of milestones. The TC will be chaired by the Technical Manager.  
Exploitation 
Committee 
(ExC) 
Coordinates all exploitation issues by the implementation and update the Exploitation Plan. It follows the marketability of t he work done in the 
implementation and will ensure that circular business criteria (profitability, effectiveness, efficiency and su stainability) will be prioritized. For this 
purpose, the ExC continuously analyses the market and ensures that the project has the capability to develop innovative strat egies, models, 
products, and services, during its lifetime. ExC consists of a one deleg ate of each industrial partner (SME or Large industry) and will be chaired 
by the Coordinator´s representative. The decisions taking and voting procedures are described in the Consortium Agreement. In addition, the ExC 
ensures that dissemination & communication activities complement the exploitation and intellectual property strategy of A2C.   
Project Management Board (PMB) 
Project Coordinator (Ms. Fuensanta Monzó, R&D Project Manager at CETEC, see CV in Section 4 -5). She will organise project management 
meetings and will coordinate payments to partners. She will have an active role in the project, taking part in all key project aspects, following-
up & adaptation the project plan & progress monitoring on all WPs. Setting management procedures. She will ensure the work programme is kept 
to schedule and objectives, deliverables and milestones are met. She will monitor the obligations compliance of all parties. She will be responsible 
for monitoring and implementing contingency actions. She will be the direct link to EC communications. 
Project Manager: Mr. Federico Mesa, (Project Manager at CETEC, CV in Section 4). He has a vast experience and knowledge in financial and 
administrative requirements of H2020 projects. He has the role to manage all day -to-day administrative aspects of the project, providing advice 
regarding financial and procedural issues and keeping track of all important administrative procedures. He will also undertake assistance duties 
such as facilitating meetings, providing logistic, review deliverables, compiling reports, disseminating documentation, etc.  
Technical Manager: Ms. Presentación García, (Technology coordinator of CTNC, CV in Section 4) who has a vast experience in R&D projects 
of multidisciplinary complexity in biotechnology, food & biology fields will be responsible for the project technical decisions. She will coordinate the 
scientific and innovation activities among the technical partners. She will monitor the status and progress of all R&I activities. She will report within 
the project structure about the progress of the technical tasks and for identifying potential risks, discussing act ions and following them up inside 
the technical WPs.  
Systemic Approach Manager : Ms. Maite Ferrando  (Managing Director at KVC, CV in Section 4) as expert on innovation, social policy and 
wellbeing, she will ensure that both holistic and circular approaches will be considered in all project implementation tasks and set replication 
objectives will be meet. 
Outreach Manager: Ms. Giuliana Folco (Research and Exploitation Manager at ICONS, CV in Section 4) who has long experience in managing 
international R&D projects of multidisciplinary complexity, will be responsible for dissemination decisions . She will make sure that the desired 
project outcomes are clearly specified and delivered to the right industry players, scientific communities, relevant authorit ies and civil society. 
Further, she will ensure the exploitation of results by means of effective management of all knowledge and Intellectual Property Right issues. She 
will ensure that the project addresses the requirements of the end -users and has the expected impact, consistent with the perspectives of the 
industrial partners i n the consortium. She also  will coordinate an outreach local desk  (lead by PRIMA) focused on maximize impacts at 
local/regional level with concrete actions. In addition, the Outreach Manager will be in charge of the Exploitation Committee.  
WP Leaders: are responsible for day-to-day operational decisions of the project. Each WP is further subdivided into tasks, which are allocated to 
Task Leathers responsible for task coordination. The Work Package Leader monitors the task progress, approves progress report and deliverables, 
assesses milestones, and deals with technical problems that concern WPs. Any changes to the members of the Work Packages Leaders shall be 
subject to approval by the GA. 
Stakeholder 
Panel (SP) Panel stakeholder is created to bring together partners and representatives of organizations, industrial companies, associations which are relevant 
in the A2C’s results uptake. The Panel will make recommendations on the necessary features of the project’ results, as well a s on the Systemic 
Circular Solution. In add ition, stakeholders will contribute to build new market routes and implementation vehicles in different industrial sectors. 
Related to the demonstration activities, online meetings and workshops for the Stakeholders Panel will be organized at EU lev el, to gain specific 
feedback from this Panel in the A2C targeted sectors. During the project implementation, new stakeholders will be contacted by KVC as Systemic 
Approach Manager to join the stakeholders’ network of A2C and they are invited to join one project meeting per year where possible. Right now

3.2.2. DECISION-MAKING MECHANISMS 
The consortium has agreed o n an organizational structure (Table 51) and decision-making mechanisms that have 
proved to be appropriate and efficient in previous H2020 projects. The responsibilities of the various management 
bodies, the decision-making process, conflict resolution, etc. will be described in detail in the Consortium Agreement 
(model DESCA), which will be signed by all partners before the official project start. Each partner will be responsible 
for effective and economic execution & management of its own activities according to the Grant Agreement and 
Consortium Agreement requirements, conditions and guidelines. To further ensure smooth interaction and 
collaboration, specific attention will be paid to: (i) internal communication flow.  GA meetings: face-to-face 
plenary consortium meetings organized every 6 months  to discuss strategic issues relating to the project and its 
progress, harmonize activities, solve potential conflicts and decide on major issues. ; PMB meetings: physical 
meetings (every 6 months) combined with the GA meetings every 6 months and intermedi ate virtual meetings 
utilizing Google Meet or similar (every 3 months). Even though the PMB is composed of WP leaders, all partners 
may be invited to the meetings and all partners will provide input to the WP leaders on the progress achieved. ; WP 
meetings: whenever deemed necessary by the WP leader, combined with the GA and PMB face -to-face meetings 
where appropriate or through Google Meet. ; Web-based communication: consisting of an external, public website 
and an internal, password-restricted web-based shared working environment as well as a dedicated Meet group. All 
relevant project documents (reports, meeting minutes presentations, etc.) will be uploaded to the internal site and the 
project members will be able to access, download and upload data and documents. The website will be fully 
operational in month 4. ; Day-to-day communication between the partners will mainly take place by online systems 
such as Meet, phone and e -mail. The Project Manager will actively stimulate and facilitate the co mmunication and 
interaction between partners.  (ii) reporting . Reporting and technical reviews: The performance of all work 
processes will be systematically monitored by the Coordinator and measured against the defined deliverables and 
milestones to ensure that the project stays focused and to identify any opportunities for improvement. Progress, 
periodic and final reports: The Project Coordinator assisted by the Project Manager will request the required input 
65 
 
and each partner will be required to report on t he work carried out and results obtained and any related delays, as 
well as on the work planned for the following period. The following reports are scheduled: - As part of its contractual 
obligation towards the EC, the consortium will deliver two Periodic Reports (financial and technical, Month 
18+60days, M36+60days) and one Final Report (M36+60days). 
-Additionally, and for internal monitoring purposes, the partners have agreed to produce intermediate internal 
progress reports (M9, M27). (iii) technical man agement. Deliverables tracking: A table of deliverables will be 
updated by the Project Manager and made available on the document sharing platform as a tracking tool. All 
deliverables will be validated by the respective WP leader, reviewed by the Project Manager, approved by the Project 
Coordinator before being distributed to the rest of the consortium, and submitted via the Portal of the EC. Technical 
review meeting(s): The Project Coordinator will make the necessary arrangements for the mandatory midterm 
review meeting by the EC Officer and external experts. (iv) financial management. The Project Coordinator will be 
responsible for the overall financial management and the timely distribution of the EC contribution. The Project 
Manager will support partners by: ①Providing detailed information on the individual budgets and H2020 financial 
rules at the project kick -off. ②Advising all partners on financial matters according to H2020 financial rules 
whenever requested (without liability). ③Monitoring expenses as part of the 9 -monthly internal progress reports. 
The PC will review and approve all financial statements and compile the overall financial data required for the two 
financial reports as part of the Periodic Reports.  (v) quality assu rance. All partners will perform their work 
according to their internal quality control and assurance procedures. At project level, a project management guide 
will be prepared, summarizing the main information for project management. It will address quality assurance aspects 
including an internal review procedure for deliverable and milestone reports. All deliverables will have to be 
reviewed by the Project manager and approved by the Project Coordinator. The achievement of milestones will be 
assessed by the Technical Committee.

(vi) conflict resolution.: The WP Leaders will assume responsibility for operational decisions within their WP, 
whereas the GA will be responsible for decisions related to strategic developments of the project.  
Procedure for decisions by the GA . Quorum: The GA shall not decide on issues unless two -thirds (2/3) of its 
members are present or represented (including attendees joining by teleconference). ①Each of the Beneficiaries has 
one vote. Absent members are not entitled to vote or transfer votes. ②Decisions will be taken by a simple majority 
of votes with the Project Coordinator holding a casting vote in the event of a tie. All partners retain a veto right.  
The details of the decision-making procedures will be laid down in the Consortium Agreement.  
Conflict resolution through a four-step procedure: Problem solving discussions and negotiations will generally take 
place during the ordinary and ad-hoc meetings between the relevant partners. If no solution can be found then: 1. The 
partners concerned will inform the WP Leader. If no solution is achieved, then; 2. The WP Leader will inform the 
Project Coordinator who will mediate between partner(s). If no solution is achieved, then; 3. The General Assembly 
will be req uired to hold an extraordinary meeting within 15 days. If the conflict can still not be resolved or if it 
significantly affects the viability or scope of the project as a whole, then; 4. Project Coordinator will then additionally 
seek advice from the EC Pr oject Officers, where appropriate. In serious situations the Project Coordinator will 
recommend that any parties in conflict conduct external mediation jointly funded by each party.  
3.2.2. INNOVATION MANAGEMENT 
The management structure and work plan propo sed follow the guidelines of the European Standard for Innovation 
Management (CEN/TS 16555 -1:2013), which provides the elements for a systematic approach to innovation and 
optimal management of aspects related to innovation capabilities.  
Innovation Management will be led by an Outreach Manager, Ms. Giuliana Folco whose main roles will be to act 
as a champion for the project and its exploitation.  
Ms. Giuliana has been nominated for this role by  the consortium as she shows strong leadership and has excellent 
cross function and cross-sectorial knowledge and skills.  
Specifically, the A2C project: ①Provides the organizational structure, communication flow and dissemination and 
exploitation plan and activities for effective innovation management. ②Brings together a consortium of partners 
with the right competences to execute a well -structured innovation program with clearly defined innovation 
objectives, assignment of roles and responsibilities, task distributions and detailed planning. ③All the required  
resources, key performance indicators, milestones and deliverables have been defined. ④Foreseen risks have been 
67 
 
listed and risk mitigation measures proposed (Section 3.2.4). ⑤The Work Plan includes the dedicated WP8, with 
tasks related to exploitation, IP  management, protection of IPR, internal and external communication and 
involvement of stakeholders. ⑥The Project Coordinator will promote a culture of knowledge sharing and innovation. 
Additionally, the E xC will guide the innovation activities by providin g insights in technical, business and market 
issues and opportunities. ⑦Advantage will be taken of the unique combination of industrial, technical & scientific 
competences in the consortium and the Stakeholder Panel to maximize the chances of bringing the project innovations 
to other similar enclaves and to establish the optimal context for the generation of novel creative ideas. 
3.2.3. RISKS RELATED TO PROJECT IMPLEMENTATION   
Risk management is  a key issue integrated in A2C  project. The following 
aspects are included in our risk analysis: Risk identification by a systemic 
approach based on the project objectives; Risk analysis, determining risk 
rating and priorisation.  We consider Risk = Likeli hood to occur x 
Severity- Likelihood to occur: Low-1, Medium-2, High-3. Severity: Low-
2, Medium-4, High-6.  Risk Level are considered: High≥12; Medium: 7-
11; Low≤6. ;Minimisation strategies: actions to minimise the likelihood to occur (Mitigation) and Contingency for 
Severity.; Risk monitoring. Each WP leader will periodically review the status of each task achievement in relation 
to its objectives. As a result of this analysis, a corrective action plan will be constructed to reiterate some of the 
tasks with changes to their content that are likely to produce an improved deliverable closer to the quantified target. 
The improved deliverable will then be re -integrated into the milestone assessmen t. The following critical risks 
(Management (M), Technical (T), External (E)) have already been considered : See their graphic representation in 
Figure 17 and see risks description in following table 3.2b. Critical risks.                           
Description of risk/Risk Level WP Proposed risk mitigation measures 
1. (T) NIAs are not adequately identified during 
the plastic recycling processes then detection 
thresholds impair return to food contact.  Low-6 
(1x6) 
1 
Mitigation: CETEC will implement a methodology for food contact assessment and compliance (task 
1.1.2.) including NIAs analysis with specific equipment able to sense ppm of pollutants.  Contingency: 
if results of identification are not successful then methodologies would be readjusted. 
2. (T) Problems in DIS integration with different 
platforms or Operative Systems (O.S.) and the 
correct visualization of the information.  Low-6 
(1x6) 
1 
Mitigation: ECO, EQU, EXU & EVRY programmers take into account the adaptive design in any O.S. 
and platform. The unification of criteria and results will be through browsers and engines that meet the 
standards and requirements of 3WC (World Wide Web Consortium). The visualization and use of DIS 
in these browsers, allows to eliminate errors from the whole system. Contingency: re-programing the 
identified problems and validating each ones.    
3. (T) The economic feasibility study determines 
a high cost in the extraction of the compounds of 
interest from vegetable wastes.  Low-6 (1x6) 
2 
Mitigation: CTNC, SSICA, DMC, CITRO & MKS will carry out a specific study for each extraction 
route determining the optimal parameters to achieve a balance between the quality of the extract, the 
environmental and economic sustainability of the system (task 2.2).  Contingency: if the routes are 
not economically viable, then studies in the variation of the key parameters will be develop. If is 
necessary alternative routes will be implemented. 
4. (T) The extracts from agrifood wastes do not 
achieve the expected purity (70-80%) and 
consequently are not valid for food, nutraceutics 
and cosmetic applications.  Low-6 (1x6) 
2 
Mitigation: SSICA, CTNC, DMC and CITRO will develop a specific route of purification for each 
extract (task 2.3) based on a synergistic combination of filtration and resins, determining the optimal 
parameters in each case.   Contingency: the parameters will be readjusted and if it is necessary 
alternative purification techniques (e.g. ion exchange chromatography) will be implemented or 
alternative agrifood wastes will be selected. 
5.(T) Feeding condition under laboratory setups 
significantly differs from industrial flows for optical 
detection.  Low-6 (1x6) 
3 
Mitigation: IRIS will establish from the beginning a common operation range flux of materials at lab 
scale and industrial level. Specific physical barriers will be designed and included if the material 
distribution on the conveyor is not considered be suitable for th e proper sorting (task 3.2). 
Contingency: If the problem is caused by either hardware or software, then additional capacity will 
be brought on line to cope with the speed. 
6. (T) PET & PE wastes do not have adequate 
characteristics (low crystallinity, molecular weight 
<500 g/mol, high polarity) to be efficiently attack 
by the customised enzymes. Low-6 (1x6) 
3 
Mitigation: CETEC will work to develop an ad -hoc pre-treatment for PE and PET wastes based on  
physic-chemical modifications (task 3.4.1) to achieve polymers chains assimilable by enzymes. 
Contingency: Others alternative pre-treatment route will be studied and designed by CETEC 
7.(T) Modification of Al-flakes not stable enough.  
Medium-8 (2x4) 3 
Mitigation: BOKU will develop two robust routes (task 3.5.2) for the Al stabilization and highly 
compatibilisation with PE matrix based on direct binding of an organic -ligand (e.g., long chai n 
carboxylic acids) that shows strong affinity to aluminium and further modification with a polyethylene 
compatible shell (e.g., polyisobutylene -PIB) and the second one based on modifications with 
aluminiumoxide/siliciumoxide in a first step, followed by t he polymer-shell synthesis.  Contingency: 
Others alternative pre-treatment routes will be studied and designed by BOKU. 
8.(T) Expected sensory quality of the new food, 
nutraceutics and cosmetic formulations 
containing the extracts are not as expected, 
being not marketable.  Low-6 (1x6) 
4 
Mitigation: DMC, CTNC, SSICA, CITRO, MCT & ALM will carry out a specific research (task 4.1 ) to 
ensure that the different extracts are idoneous for new food formulations (jams, compotes, juices, 
vegetable drinks, and vegetable creams), nutraceutical formulations (antioxidants), and antioxidants 
and antiskin aging cosmetic formulations, ensuring their functionality without compromising nutritional 
balance, physical parameters and sensory quality.  Contingency:  reformulations will be made to 
achieve the expected technical results. If it is necessary other alternative extracts and/or agri -food 
wastes will be studied. 
9.(T) Recycled plastics contains contaminants 
not being suitable for food applications.  Low-6 
(1x6) 
5 
Mitigation: WETS & CEW will implement at GWC facilities a water washing system to eliminate 
organic materials, including detection of microplastics that will be eliminated by microfiltration. 
Moreover, GWC will implement a decontamination technology (vacuum reaction) before extrusion 
process (including devolatilization ports to contribute to the decontamination) to eliminate all potential 
volatile and semi -volatile compounds and odours.  Contingency: If decontamination is not enough 
Figure 17. Risks representation

3.3. CONSORTIUM AS A WHOLE 
A2C brings a multidisciplinary team with complementary and excellent expertise. The A2C Consortium is a strong 
platform of experts along “the first territorial systemic solution for the upcycling of agrifood wastes, including 
plastics and fruits & vegetable wastes into high added value products for agrifood & cosmetic sectors”.   
Moreover, a fluent network collaboration with strategic stakeholders (e.g., some will be part of the Stakeholders 
Panel, others will participate in A2C co-creation and outreach actions such as the 26 European clusters engaged).  
The Consortium involves 10 European countries and the core is in the Region of Murcia (ES) since it is a key player 
of the European agrifood industry. Moreover, the Consortium involves other 9 European countries (GER, AT, UK, 
IT, NL, BEL, FIN, CH, LI) bringing the most advance technologies to the cluster, circular business & communication 
experts and two areas for replication (IT, LI) and addressing a balance between Southern, Northern and Eastern 
Europe.The Consortium consists of 41 partners with complementary competences as following: 
(<99%) then other alternative decont amination technologies will be studied (supercritical CO 2 during 
the extrusion) 
10.(T) Redox unbalance in the desired 
bioconversion pathways of the enzymatic 
degradation products into building blocks for 
cosmetic.  Low-6 (1x6) 
5 
Mitigation: UNIMIB  will calculate the redox balance and thermodynamics of all the reactions by 
specific tools  http://equilibrator.weizmann.ac.il/) and compensations will be applied where needed, 
such as enzyme engineering for cofactor swapping and compensatory reactions for either adding an 
electron sink or for providing reducing equivalent. Contingency: Other alternative  compensatory 
routes will be studied. 
11.(T) Morphologies obtained by 
compatibilisation by extensional flow mixing are 
lower than expected (L/W<100) not reaching high 
barrier properties.   Low-6 (1x6) 
5 
Mitigation: CETEC and GWC will implement a synergistic strategy based on specific compatibilisation 
routes carried out under extensional flow mixing during the extrusion process in task 5.2, that will be 
achieved by the incorporation of a convergent -divergent plate in the extruder.  Contingency: Other 
compatibilisers will be studied and if it is necessary other routes for the extensional flow achievement 
will be design. 
12.(T) Mismatch at the interplay between 
technologies at the ‘integration of technologies at 
pilot scale phase.  Low-6 (1x6) 
6 
Mitigation: Planned and well-coordinated communication and alignment of all technologies during the 
phases preceding the ‘integration of technologies at pilot scale’ phase. A specific task in the project 
(T6.1) will be focused in the integration of all develop technologies at pilot scale. It will be led by GWC 
in collaboration with all technical partners.  Contingency: If necessary, a pilot will be redesigned to fit 
the integrated production chain. 
13.(E) Difficulties in involving EU -wide decision-
makers and poor outreach at EU level. 
Medium-8 (2x4) 
7 
Mitigation: the participation in EU alliances and clusters  (already engaged through support letters)  
will facilit ate the EU -wide involvement ; however, a potential suboptimal outreach should be 
considered: all partner s will devote significant efforts in maximizing the project impact and, in 
collaboration with WP8 leaders and the Outreach Manager , resources and means will be put at 
disposal of the whole consortium for fostering an optimal communication and involvement o f relevant 
European stakeholders.  Besides, EURA as the representative of European regional development 
agencies, has strong links with decision makers and networks at EU level   Contingency: Increase 
efforts and using the networks of stakeholders that are being engaged.  
14.(E) Low citizenship engagement and 
suboptimal involvement of relevant stakeholders 
in the participatory processes. Low-6 (1x6) 
7 
Mitigation: although socio -economic and socio -cultural conditions of all communities targeted may 
undermine the recruitment and engagement process, an in -depth revision of concurring factors and 
potential solutions will be conducted prior the implementation of the WP7 actions; also, the iterative 
process of assessment and the continuous surveillance of the publ ic engagement strategy will allow 
to adapt the actions and measures in a timely manner ). Besides, PRIMA, the leader of the actions, 
has strong links at community levels and will be supported by the Alhama de Murcia municipality 
(support letter) in carrying  out the participative action and engage citizens. Contingency: e.g., to 
involve more CSOs in touch with the communities, community leaderships and community business 
for aiding the engagement. 
15.(E) Low performance of the communication 
activity and suboptimal audience outreach. .  
Low-6 (1x6) 
8 
Mitigation: WP8 leader ICONS has vast experience in outreach actions and together with involved 
partners will evaluate the strategy and the performance of actions yearly; for communication 
campaigns, there will be a baseline and final evaluation. This iterative approach allows to detect and 
make corrective actions ahead on time in order to maximise the outreach of the activities and the 
A2Cscope.  Contingency: re-edition of the A2C Dissemination & Communication strategy. 
16.(E) It is not sufficiently ensured that the 
developed technologies, processes, etc. align to 
the latest stand ards, which could lead to 
incompatibility with already existing solutions and 
thus threaten a successful entry into the market .    
Medium-8 (2x4) 
8 
Mitigation: Right from the start of the project, it is made sure that all relevant standards are taken into 
account and that no stand-alone solutions are being developed but fit into the market/already existing 
solutions. Contingency: The compliance with most relevant standards will be checked at several 
stages in the project. 
17.(M) Delays in the execution of tasks/WP or 
deliverables cause delays in project expected 
progress. Medium-8 (2x4) 
9 
Mitigation: Work package leaders and tasks leaders have been selected based on a wide experience 
in relation to the project activities. Project Management and decision mechanisms in Consortium 
Agreement (task 1.1). Contingency: If is necessary the Project Coordinator will reallocate some tasks 
to avoid delays. 
18.(M) A partner leaves the project or 
underperforms either technically or financially. 
Low-6 (1x6) 
9 
Mitigation: Exhaustive control of activities,  consortium with agreed and negotiated tasks, meditated 
and measured tasks and efforts. Consortium agreement. Contingency: Substitution by other partner 
with similar profile. In addition, the whole capabilities of each partner have been explored and partial  
tasks could even be done by current partners (same or different departments/areas). 
19.(M) Lack of overall coordination. Low-6 (1x6) 9 
Mitigation: Effective coordination ensured by the management structure and the work plan. The 
project Coordinator has a  vast experience in coordinating EU projects and is supported by the 
executive board. Contingency: Staff in charge of the project will be re -evaluated and will be carried 
out the reallocation of the tasks and personnel efforts. 
20.(M) Delays in the samples reception due 
borders closing for Covid-19. Medium-8 (2x4) 9 Mitigation: Activities will be plan taking into account time allotted to accomplish the calendar.   
Contingency: In case of long periods then we will focus on other specific aspects of the project.

Plastic multilayers upcycling value chain 
CETEC (ES) will lead the related developments in collaboration with IRIS (ES) optical sorting, SAPE (DE) physical delamination, MELLI 
(UK) enzymatic depolymerisation, GWC(ES) decontamination, mechanical recycling & new compound s, UNIMIB (IT) biotransformation of 
enzymatic degradation products into high added value substances for cosmetics, CETBIO (ES) & UA (ES) PHBV bioplastics & carotenoids 
production. GWC will be the leader of the integration of all technologies at pilot scale in a demonstrator. 
Valorisation of the agrifood waste value chain 
CTNC (ES) will lead the related developments in collaboration with DMC (ES) green extraction+enzymatic hydrolysis+microwave-assisted 
extraction, MKSI (IT) microwave extraction technology developer, CITRO (ES) green extraction+ultrasound-assisted extraction, SSICA (IT) 
purification and stabilisation of the bioactive extracts . The wastes providers for the developments in both value chains will be MCT (ES), 
ALM (ES), CITRO (ES), multilayer packaging & agrifood wastes and PROEX (ES) multilayer agricultural films & agrifood wastes.  
Digital tool DIS for the agrifood sector 
ECO (ES) leading related developments, in collaboration with EQU (ES) watermark impression, EXUS (LI) Big Data, EVRY (LI) blockchain. 
End users to validate the A2C developments in a real environment  
SOLP (ES) new recyclable barrier films & biodegradable films for agriculture, EVER (ES) barrier packaging and biodegradable packaging, 
LOL (ES) new cosmetic formulations, MCT (ES), ALM (ES), CITRO (ES) new food formulations and DMC (ES) new cosmetic formulations 
Sustainability approach 
REG (ES) will ensure the energetic sustainability and WETS (NL) & CEW (NL) the water sustainability of all A2C processes, and  VTT (FI) 
will perform the LCA, measuring cluster circularity and benchmarking of solutions.  
A2C Systemic approach and multidimensional model for adoption, replication & scalability and A2C Outreach  
KVC(ES, public engagement, socioeconomics) will lead the related activities in collaboration with experts on SSH disciplines, UVEG (ES) 
public engagement, socioeconomics and p olicy, AGRO(ES) leading Murcia CEAP, regional socioeconomics, PRIMA (ES) leading 
local/regional engagement, regional socioeconomics, PROEX (ES) regional socioeconomics, CJM (ES) private financing, UB (IT) CE 
expert, A2C CEBMs and socioeconomics, VTT (FI) environmental, circularity & benchmarking, CARM (ES) public administration, regional 
policy and public financing, INFO (ES) public administration, public financing, UNE(ES) standardisation organism, EURA (BE) leading 
clustering actions, public European fund s & policy, TCA (IT) & LPK(LT) replication cases, ICONS (IT) leading A2C Outreach, A2C 
exploitation.

4.MEMBERS OF THE CONSORTIUM
4.1 PARTICIPANTS 
4.1.1  CETEC – CENTRO TECNOLÓGICO DEL CALZADO Y DEL PLÁSTICO  
 
PARTNER Nº: 1 (RTO) 
WEBSITE: www.ctcalzado.org 
SHORTNAME: CETEC  
LOCATION: Spain 
ROLE IN THE PROJECT: PROJECT COORDINATOR. 
 
DESCRIPTION OF THE LEGAL ENTITY  
 
CETEC is a non -profit organization, founded in 1994 and supported by the regional administration and regional 
manufacturers, with the mission of improving the competitiveness of the regional SMEs and companies in the 
footwear and plastic sector. Currently, it is formed by almost 70 SMEs and companies of footwear and plastic areas. 
CETEC is a meeting point to carry R&D project, acquire legal information, regional and national funding for projects, 
among other activities. 
For this purpose, the company is organized in four departments: (1) Administration and Management, (2) R&D, (3) 
Laboratory and Quality and (4) Technical Consultancy, in charge of the following activities: 
▪ Conducting R&D leading to transfer processes. 
▪ Promoting the implementation of innovative technologies in business. 
▪ Generating and disseminating technological knowledge to companies devoted to similar activities. 
▪ Collaborating and promoting standardization processes. 
▪ Disseminating the values of technology in the environment economic and social of the centre. 
▪ Ensuring appropriate advice and technical assistance in those areas that are particularly sensitive to the 
competitive development: i) Quality control, ii) Product development and industrial design, iii) Industrial 
organization and production, iv) Automation and industrial robotics. 
 
The main CETEC research areas are: formulation & compounding of bioplastics and biodegradable materials, 
new bioplastics for packaging applications, development of composites & nanocomposites , development of 
bioplastics formulations with natural additives, acceleration of biodegradation properties of polymers and 
development of formulations for high performance plastics and multilayer structures (barrier, thermal, mechanical & 
optical properti es), new alternatives for plastics/bioplastics recycling  and recycling studies and manufacturing 
processes (injection, thermoforming, cast & blown extrusion).  
 
CETEC is an associate member of the Bio-based Industries Consortium (BIC) and a member of the Network of 
Technological Centres in the Region of Murcia (CECOTEC) which is recognized as Results Transfer Office for 
the Government of Spain. Furthermore, CETEC is a full member of The Bio-Based Industries Joint Undertaking 
(BBI JU), that is a Public-Private Partnership between the EU and the Bio-based Industries Consortium. 
 
MAIN TASKS IN THE PROJECT 
 
CETEC is the Coordinator of the project, being in charge of assisting other partners in the development of their 
activities. CETEC will lead the WP 9-Project Management & Coordination . CETEC will also be involved in 
WP1, leading A2C requirements (T1.1), and A2C methodologies tasks (T1.2) and developing the plastics multilayers 
flows characterisation (T1.4.). In WP3, characterizing the plastics flows from the physical delamination (T3.3), 
developing pre-treatments to the PET/PE multilayers, in collaboration with GWC, to enhance the enzymatic attack,  
developing blends by extrusion of the modified aluminium with LDPE/EVOH/LDPE and LDPE/PA/LDPE matrix 
and developing processable  LDPE/EVOH/LDPE, LDPE/EVOH, LDPE/PA/LDPE, LDPE/PA, LDPE, PET 
compounds (T3.5). In WP5, compatibilisation and extensional flow mixing strategies for development of high barrier 
compounds (T5.2), collaboration with GWC in the develop of PHBV biodegradable compounds (T5.3), 
transformation of plastics compounds into food packaging & agricultur al films at small scale and validation, 
recyclability, compostability & biodegradability studies (T5.4). In WP6, will be involved in the A2C demonstrators 
(T6.2), in setting the basis for future industrial implementation (T6.3). Moreover, CETEC will be involved in WP8 
in communication & dissemination activities (T8.2, 8.4, 8.5, 8.6,8.7). 
 
Project Management experience : CETEC experience as coordinator began in FP7 being promotors & technical 
coordinators of GREENAVOID (8 partners; FP7 -SME-2011-BSG;2012-2015) & DEGRICOL (9 partners, FP7 -

Section 4,5,6-page 4 
 
SME-2012; 2012-2015). In H2020 frame, CETEC has coordinated the project HTPush (H2020-NMP-25-SMEInst-
2-2014; 2014 -2016. Universal and compatible system for plumbing and heating), the project BIOMULCH (5 
partners; H2020-FTIPilot-2016; Integrated solution for innovative biodegradation control of agricultural plastic 
mulches; 2017-2019) and the project AppShoe (Erasmus+ KA3-EACEA40-2016; 2017-2019),  H2020 projects have 
been successful projects obtaining real demonstrators and base for new projects (currently CETEC is involved in the 
submission of BIODIS, that is the evolution of BIOMULCH, as Project Coordinator). 
Currently, CETEC is the Coordinator of project upPE-T, funded by H2020-NMBP-TR-IND-2018-2020, Upcycling 
of PE & PET wastes to generate biodegradable bioplastics for food & drink packaging  and of the project VALUE-
RUBBER, funded by H2020-EIC-FTI-2018-2020, Recycling technology to introduce rubber for End-of-Life Tyres 
into production lines as virgin rubbers substitute and of the project. 
 
Other related experience : CETEC has a vast experience on R&D, quality control and characterization, 
compounding and transformation of plastics that will be key for the project implementation. CETEC has previous 
experience in the formulation, compounding and transformation of bioplastics, such as PLA and PHA, for food 
packaging & agriculture applications, recyclability and biodegradation studies. Moreover, they have experience in 
the plastics pre-treatment for enhance the enzymatic attack and prove of it is their participation in the project upPE-
T (H2020-NMBP-TR-IND-2018-2020) where CETEC decrease crystallinity, polarity and molecular weight of PE & 
PET wastes.  CETEC has a fully -equipped plastic laboratory and a complete pilot plant for plastic formulation, 
compounding and transformation.  
 
INTEREST IN THE PROJECT 
 
CETEC participation in A2C project will broad its experience as Coordinator and expand its European network, 
being involved in advance technologies for plastic wastes upcycling. In particular, CETEC will be pioneer in the 
development of new high barrier plastics compounds for food packaging and agriculture as alternative to current 
multilayers and-hoc pre-treatments to enhance enzymatic attack of PE/PET mix plastic wastes. CETEC will transfer 
knowledge to their associated companies of the plastic and recycling sectors

4.1. 2 GWC -GREEN WORLD COMPOUNDING  
 
PARTNER Nº: 2 (SME) 
WEBSITE: http://www.gwplastics-group.com/ 
SHORTNAME: GWC 
LOCATION: Spain 
ROLE IN THE PROJECT: PARTNER. 
 
DESCRIPTION OF THE LEGAL ENTITY  
 
Green World Compounding (GWC)  is a company producer of sustainable compounds and masterbatches 
from agricultural and industrial plastic waste.  GWC is specialized in the manufacturing of recycled products 
based on polypropylene (PP), polyethylene (PE), being one of the leading companies in Europe in the manufacturing 
of reinforced glass recycled polyethylene and polypropylene compounds. Moreover,  GWC is the leading company 
of recycled plastics from agricultural and industrial waste sources 
on a national basis. 
GWC belongs to the group GW formed by : GWE (Green World 
Enterprise), which is dedicated to the recycling and trading of 
plastic waste (poly propylene, polyethylene terephthalate and 
polyethylene) and GWC dedicated to the manufacturing of 
recycled compounds and masterbatches.  
GWC is dedicated to the continuous improvement by means of an 
intensive labour on R+D in order to be able to control th e quality 
variations of plastic waste and obtain on demand formulations to 
produce sustainable compounds and masterbatches to be used in 
specific applications.  
MAIN TASKS IN THE PROJECT 
 
GWC is involved in WP1, A2C requirements (T1.1), collaboration in me thodologies for plastics food contact 
assessment & compliance to agriculture standards (T1.2), and leading with PROEX the A2C residues management 
plan. GWC leads WP3, where they deal with the plastics wastes pre -treatments & preliminary decontamination 
(T3.1), monitoring the sorting system coupled with the multilayer materials treatments (T3.2), sorting of physically 
delaminated materials (T3.3), collaboration with CETEC in PET/PE plastics pre-treatments to enhance the enzymatic 
attack, plastics decontamination & collaboration in the development of processable plastics compounds (T3.5), and 
also will lead WP6, managing the integration of A2C technologies at pilot scale (T6.1) and the demonstration of all 
the technologies in a relevant and industrial environment (T6.2), setting the basis for the futur e industrial 
implementation (T6.3). Moreover, GWC will be involved in WP8 in communication & dissemination activities 
(T8.2, 8.4, 8.5, 8.6,8.7). 
 
Related experience : GWC, as a leader plastics recycling facility, has a vast experience in plastics wastes pre -
treatment, cleaning, mechanical recycling of packaging and agricultural films: moreover, they develop formulations 
for the development of recycled compounds with enhanced properties, addressing the plastic waste problem through 
innovation. The GWC team skillset and vision are extremely relevant to the work the A2C consortium will carry out. 
 
INTEREST IN THE PROJECT 
 
GWC participation in A2C will allow them the implementation of the first plant for the recycling of simple and 
complex multilayers containing aluminium in Europe, promoting a new business line in the circular economy and 
being pioneers and enlarging its portfolio of products and clients. Moreover, they will broad its European networking 
with other relevant stakeholders in the Circular Economy and plastic waste sectors.

4.1.3 SAPE -SAPERATEC  
 
• PARTNER Nº: 3 (SME) 
• WEBSITE: www.saperatec.de 
• SHORTNAME: SAPE  
• LOCATION: Germany 
• ROLE IN THE PROJECT: PARTNER. 
DESCRIPTION OF THE LEGAL ENTITY  
 
Saperatec is the first company in Europe specialised in separate the Aluminium from post -consumer 
PE/Al/PET packages like stand-up pouches by physical delamination based on separating fluids, allowing obtain 
individual materials (PE, Aluminium y PET) with high quality. 
Saperatec has been founded in 2010 with the intension to exploit the patented Saperatec technology as new 
innovative recycling process for multilayer materials. As one of the first application fields, Saperatec started its 
business with the aim to recycle of thin film photovoltaic modules. The development of a photovoltaic -recycling 
pilot line was partially funded by the Germa n DBU Project no. 29682 (11/2011 -11/2012). After installation of the 
pilot line the company acted as photovoltaic recycling company for a period of appr. 12 months. Due to the strong 
withdrawal of the photovoltaic production in Europe the photovoltaic recycling market has been decreased 
dramatically in short-term forcing Saperatec to change its business field. The comprehensive experience acquired by 
using the separation liquids for the separation of photovoltaic modules could be transferred to other materials to be 
recycled. In 2013, Saperatec build a flexible Pilot Recycling Plant to further exploit the identified application fields. 
A comprehensive market study revealed that the market of flexible packaging is a timely, realistic and promising 
business opportunity. As for PE/Al/PET packages, like stand -up pouches.  In 2014, Saperatec’s technology has 
been awarded with the Green Tec Award, Europe’s most renowned environmental and business prize, in the 
category “Recycling & Resources”. In 2016 Saperatec has been added to the Global Cleantech 100 list – a yearly 
award for companies expected to have the highest market  impact in the next 5 -10 years. Currently, Saperatec is in 
the engineering phase for the operation of the first industrial recycle plant for flexible composite packaging. 
MAIN TASKS IN THE PROJECT 
 
SAPE will be involved in WP3, developing a key A2C task the physical separation of complex multilayers containing 
aluminium (T3.3) to obtain the separated flows: LDPE/PET, LLDPE/PET, LDPE, PET and Aluminium. In WP6 will 
be involved in the integration of th e developed technology at pilot scale in the final A2C demonstrator (T6.1) . 
Moreover, they will be involved in WP8 in communication & dissemination activities (T8.2, 8.4, 8.5, 8.6,8.7). 
 
Related experience: SAPE is the unique developed technology in Europe for the separation of aluminium from 
complex multilayers. The principle to separate aluminium from multilayer systems by the use of a separation liquids 
has been investigated for more than 10 years by the researcher Dr. Horst Seibt, co -founder and shareholder of 
Saperatec.  We have specific experience that will be key for the development of A2C tasks: fluids design & 
characterisations, fluid production, delamination testing, engineering capabilities (P&ID, mass balance calculations). 
INTEREST IN THE PROJECT 
 
By participating in A2C project, SAPE will adapt its technology to post -industrial materials containing aluminium 
broading its knowledge and being the first plant in Europe able to delaminate post-industrial complex multilayers, 
establishing new markets for Saperatec technology . Moreover, they will broad its European networking with other 
relevant stakeholders in the Circular Economy and plastic waste sectors.  
KEY PERSONNEL 
 
 Dr. Sebastian Kernbaum (male). He is the Managing Director of Saperatec and has a n experience of over 20 
years in plastics recycling. Ing. Mechanical Engineering and Production Technology at TU Berlin; Master and 
Doctoral Thesis in Recycling Planning and Control, expert in Re-Use of Electrical and Electronic Equipment. 
 Dr. Marcus Schulze (male). Head of R&D at Saperatec. He is a plastics expert with a PhD in Organic Chemistry 
by Würzburg University.  He has more than ten years of experience in the international plastics industry. 
 Dr. Dennis Meisel (male).  R & Development technician at Saperatec. He holds a Chemistry degree. He has 
specific experience related to the plastics formulations and characterisation at laboratory.  
 Mr. Jörg Uhding (male). Process engineering at Saperatec. He is an expert in Conceptual Design of Recycling 
plants, and has a vast experience (10 years) working with plastics packaging in project planning and execution.

INFRASTRUCTURE AND/OR ANY MAJOR ITEMS OF TECHNICAL EQUIPMENT 
 
Saperatec ope rates at it’s headquarters offices, lab infrastructure and a pilot plant for developing recycling 
technologies for multilayer materials based on separation fluids / the delamination technology.  
 
All R&D activities are currently performed in 2 Saperatec labs . One is dedicated to th e liquid development and 
optimization, the other acts as an intermediate between the liquid development and the pilot line. In the latter, 
separation trials are executed in 3 litres environments, added by all relevant pre-test before entering the pilot line (1,5 
m³). Besides that, the lab is equipped especially with means for fluid development and analysis, including HPLC, 
and Photometer.  
 
The pilot plant is designed for batch 
operation of small quantities ranging 
from 30 up to 200 kg feed material 
(depending on material type). The 
storage capacity for the waste 
composite materials (input) is 
maximal 90 Tons. The treatment of the 
composite materials is carried out with 
separation liquid. The liquid consists 
of water and other additives such as 
acids and bases. The pilot line is 
subdivided in six departments: pre -
treatment, Saperatec core process, 
recovery of liquids, mechanical 
separation, media, storage. T he picture 
shows our pilot plant.

nanotechnology in Austria .  BIMat specializes in biological systems a nd materials, including polymer

4.1.6 MELLI -MELLIZYME BIOTECHNOLOGY LTD  
 
PARTNER Nº: 6 (SME) 
WEBSITE: www.mellizyme.com  
SHORTNAME: MELLI 
LOCATION: United Kingdom 
ROLE IN THE PROJECT: PARTNER.  
 
DESCRIPTION OF THE LEGAL ENTITY  
 
Mellizyme is a privately owned biotech start-up founded by CEO Jacob Nathan and CSO Douglas Kell (scientific 
leader at University of Liverpool) in 2019. They develop cutting edge tools that use synthetic biology to engineer 
and optimise enzymes. Mellizyme discovered the only known enzyme to degrade previously difficult to recycle 
polymers, those that have a  carbon-carbon backbone such as polyethylene (PE). Building on this discovery 
Mellizyme is using its cutting-edge protein engineering platform, that relies on synthetic biology, automation and 
machine learning techniques, to optimise the performance of this enzyme so it can be employed to recycle plastics.  
 
MAIN TASKS IN THE PROJECT 
 
MELLI will contribute heavily to WP3 by leading subtask 3. 5.2 “Engineering and Characterising a PE/PET 
degrading enzyme”, where they will engineer and characterise an enzyme capable of degrading PE/PET polymers. 
MELLI will also lead on subtask 3.5.3., “Scale -up of PE/PET degrading enzyme manufacture and enzymatic 
degradation of PE/PET”, where they will scale up manufacturing of the engineered enzyme as well as the process for 
degrading PE/PET. In WP6 MELLI will implement their degradation process in a 50 L pilot demonstration process 
in Spain, where they will degra de PE/PET and recover valuable products. Moreover, MELLI will be involved in 
WP8 in communication & dissemination activities (T8.2, 8.4, 8.5, 8.6,8.7). 
 
Related experience: MELLI discovered the only known enzyme to degrade previously difficult to recycle polymers, 
those that have a carbon-carbon backbone such as polyethylene (PE) and polyesters as PET. 
 
INTEREST IN THE PROJECT 
 
Mellizyme are interested in the Agro2Circular project for a number of reasons. First, the funding would enable us 
to demonstrate that we can use our protein engineering platform to optimize our enzyme for a specific application. 
Second, our involvement in Agro2Circular is a chance to exemplify that our plastic degrading enzyme can be used 
to reduce plastic waste, create valuable chemical feedstocks and be plugged into a circular economy. Finally, for 
our plastic degrading enzyme to be deployed at scale it needs to be part of a wider supply  chain (or circle in this 
case). Engaging in this project is an invaluable opportunity for Mellizyme to build relationships with other members 
of the consortium and integrate our technologies to build a wider circular system. In the future we hope to build on 
these relationships further by applying our joint circular solution at an even larger scale and contributing to solving 
the plastics crisis, combatting the climate and ecological emergency (CEE) and bringing about systemic change to 
the way we manage plastic waste and manufacture chemicals.

RELEVANT PUBLICATIONS, PRODUCTS, SERVICES, OR OTHER ACHIEVEMENTS 
 
Platform for engineering plastic degrading enzymes. Our experimental platform for engineering proteins is based 
on a set of proven “synthetic biology” methods pioneered by Mellizyme’s CSO Professor Douglas Kell, and Senior 
Computational researcher Dr Neil Swainston, as is demonstrated by the fact they’ve been published in peer-reviewed 
journals. Initially, sequences of DNA holding information that bacteria can use to produce a large set (>10^5), or 
library, of  different variations of an enzyme are designed using software GeneGenie 1. Next, a lab process, 
SpeedyGenes, is used to assemble the  DNA sequences that code for the library designed in GeneGenie 2. 
Subsequently, the protein library is tested to discover the best enzyme variants, which in the case of this project are 
the ones that best degrade multilayer plastics. Subsequently, the DNA sequences encoding  the “best enzymes” are 
sequenced. Knowledge of how the DNA sequence affects enzyme performance is learnt from and used to inform a  
second “round” of directed evolution, where the enzyme optimised in the first round is subject to further rounds of 
evolution, until an enzyme is found that carries out our desired function to standards we define3,4.  
1. Swainston, Neil, Andrew Currin, Philip J. Day, and Douglas B. Kell. ‘GeneGenie: Optimized Oligomer Design for Directed Evolut ion’. Nucleic Acids Research 42, no. W1 (1 July 2014): W395 –400. 
https://doi.org/10.1093/nar/gku336.  
2. Currin, Andrew, Neil Swain ston, Philip J. Day, and Douglas B. Kell. ‘SpeedyGenes: An Improved Gene Synthesis Method for the Efficient Production of Err or-Corrected, Synthetic 
Protein Libraries for Directed Evolution’. Protein Engineering, Design and Selection 27, no. 9 (September 2 014): 273–80. https://doi.org/10.1093/protein/gzu029.  
3. Currin, Andrew, Neil Swainston, Philip J. Day, and Douglas B. Kell. ‘Synthetic Biology for the Directed Evolution of Protein Biocatalysts: Navigating Sequence Space Intelligently’. Chemical Society 
Reviews 44, no. 5 (2015): 1172–1239. https://doi.org/10.1039/C4CS00351A.  
4. Sadler, Joanna C., Lucy Green, Neil Swainston, Douglas B. Kell, and Andrew Currin. ‘Fast and Flexible Synthesis of Combinatorial Libraries for Directed Evolution’. In Methods in Enzymology, 608:59–
79. Elsevier, 2018. https://doi.org/10.1016/bs.mie.2018.04.006.

4.1.7 CETBIO -CETEC BIOTECHNOLOGY, SL

DESCRIPTION OF THE LEGAL ENTITY  
CETEC Biotechnology (CETBIO), is a new spin-off from the Technological Center of Footwear and Plastic of 
the Region of Murcia (CETEC). CETBIO was born out in 2020 of the essential belief that success of a company is 
linked to a firm commitment towards sustainability and protection of the environment. CETBIO is a company focus 
in the application of biotechnological processes and approaches for enhancing biodegradation of plastics in the 
environment and its valorization as wel l as for the industrial production, formulation and manufacturing of 
biodegradable bioplastics, especially polyhydroxyalkanoates (PHA) biopolymers.  

Section 4,5,6-page 18 
 
CETBIO has been funded after over 25 years of research at  CETEC Technological Center whose more 
relevant findings, protocols and methods have been transferred to the company 
One of the main objectives of CETBIO is to make biodegradable bioplastics competitive in environmental, economic 
and performance-related terms. The viable solution strategy of CETBIO is the utilization of residues as a feedstock 
for the biotechnological process. Actually, CETEC has signed relevant agreements with regional agri-food companies 
for the supply of industrial solid wastes for the exploitation of these wastes as energy a nd carbon sources for the 
biotechnological production of PHA. 
CETBIO has invested in state -of-the-art facilities and equipment as well as highly qualified human resources with 
the vision to bring its products and services to market and provide a sustainabl e and economic alternative to 
conventional plastics.

The University of Milano -Bicocca is a multidisciplinary University where teaching (providing undergraduate, 
graduate and post -graduate education), research and technology transfer are pursued and offered to about 33.000 
students. The scientific team of the Department of Biotechnology and  Biosciences is composed of about 50

KEY PERSONNEL 
 
 Dra Paola Branduardi (female). She is a graduated cum Laude in Biological Sciences at the University of 
Milano, Italy, and received a PhD in Cellular and Molecular Biology at the University of Milano, with an 
internship at the Vienna BioCenter, working on the yeast cell cycle progressi on. She moved in 2000 at the 
University of Milano Bicocca as Post-Doc, where she started to work on Industrial Biotechnology and she is now 
appointed as full professor in Chemistry of Fermentation and Industrial Microbiology. Paola’s group is interested 
in the development of sustainable microbial -based bioprocesses, mainly valorizing residual biomasses as in the 
concept of biorefineries. This is pursued by tailoring microbial strains, mainly but not exclusively Saccharomyces 
and non- Saccharomyces yeasts, for the production of fine and bulk chemicals, biofuels, nutraceuticals. Synthetic 
biology, metabolic engineering screening protocols and adaptive laboratory evolution are the approaches used to 
leverage microbial potential, including robustness against stress, to match industrial requirements. She published 
over 60 peer -reviewed papers, 7 book chapters, and she is (co -)inventor of 11 patent applications, 7 of which 
obtained the PCT status, and 5 were subsequently licensed. 
 Dr. Maximum Labra (male). Full professor at Department of biotechnology.. He has a documented experience 
in general and systematic botany and in plant molecular biology. His main research lines concern: Analysis of the 
genetic variability of spontaneous and cultivated species for their cha racterization and conservation. Evaluation 
of agroecosystems in order to study sustainable development strategies. Analysis of food quality and traceability 
of agri -food chains through the use of molecular DNA markers.  Study of food production processes an d the 
microbiome to implement food quality and determine their geographical origin. alorisation of waste from 
agricultural supply chains through phytoextraction processes and biotechnological approaches with the aim of 
obtaining bioactive compounds with high added value and supporting agro-production systems.

Paola Branduardi manages fully equipped laboratories for cellular and molecular microbiology, including genetics 
and biochemistry, and has access to a dedicated biotechnology facility called “Biotechnicum” (Bicocca Biotechnicum 
Centre, BBC), which is aimed at the development of proprietary industrial strains, fermentation and bioconversion 
processes for the production of proteins, metabolites and enzymes. More in detail, the BBC comprises fermentation 
units and rooms for shake -flasks microbial cultivation equipped for strain development and pre -pilot scale 
fermentation (4x2L -2x10L fully instrumented bioreactors, Sartorius)  in GMP -like facility, HPLC and GC units 
included. Moreover, a dedicated flow cytometer instrumentation is used for validation and optimization assays. The 
team of Industrial Microbiology and Fermentation has earlier been engaged in the production of heter ologous 
proteins, fine and bulk chemicals, including biofuels, from metabolically engineered conventional and non -
conventional yeasts and bacteria, for more than 20 years. The team has also developed, patented and licensed the 
technology for the production of lactic and ascorbic acid as well as for butanol from metabolically engineered yeasts. 
They have participated to several EU project, from different editions of framework programme, two MSCA ITN 
actions (one currently running), and two COST actions are a lso ongoing. In addition to that, several national and 
regional programmes.

research in the group range from basic research processes on biochemistry and molecular biology of 
microorganisms, including the develo pment and optimization of technologies for microbial fermentation and

DNA sequencing.
