4.1.10 WET -WETSUS - EUROPEAN CENTRE OF EXCELLENCE FOR SUSTAINABLE WATER 
TECHNOLOGY  
 
PARTNER Nº: 10 (RTO) 
WEBSITE: www.wetsus.nl 
SHORTNAME: WETS 
LOCATION: Netherlands 
ROLE IN THE PROJECT: PROJECT COORDINATOR. 
 
DESCRIPTION OF THE LEGAL ENTITY  
 
Stichting Wetsus, European Centre of Excellence For Sustainable Water Technology, is a research institute dedicated 
to sustainable water technology. At WETSUS, a unique environment is created where over 100 companies and 23 
European universities participate in creating innovative solutions to water-related problems. The institute carries out 
multidisciplinary research performed by 60 PhD students and postdoctoral researchers who are mostly located in the 
WETSUS laboratories in Leeuwarden, the Netherlands. WETSUS is part of WaterCampus Leeuwarden.  
MAIN TASKS IN THE PROJECT 
 
WETS will be involved in WP1, establishing in collaboration with CEW a strategy for water efficiency across A2C 
processes (T1.3) . In WP3 they will develop  in collaboration with CEW  the near zero liquid discharge water 
management facility focussed on water recovery (reverse osmose, ultrafiltration), micro-plastics removal and organic 
resource recovery (T3.1), by-products valorisation of enzymatic process (T3.5.3). In WP5 WETS will focus on the 
recovery of PHBV from the salty PHBV rich biomass. Wetsus will supply the design of the down-stream processing 
at pilot scale including process steps of cell lysis, dewatering and drying. The PHBV is extracte d at the solvent 
extraction pilot at Wetsus , and they will collaborate with CEW in the PHBV by -products valorisation (T5.1.2). In 
WP6 they will be involved in the integration of the developed technology at pilot scale in the final A2C demonstrator 
(T6.1). Moreover, they will be involved in WP8 in communication & dissemination activities (T8.2, 8.4, 8.5, 8.6,8.7). 
Related experience: WETS has the personnel, expertise and facilities to support the development and upscaling of 
novel technologies in the field o f sustainable water technology. WETS is located at the water campus where it has 
access to facilities for piloting and demonstration of water treatment installations. Experiments to support the 
upscaling work can be done in the WETS laboratories. The resea rchers have the support of competent technicians 
and analysts. The WETS research network and Water campus network are well organized and well equipped for 
complex and multidisciplinary projects. WETSUS is dedicated to transfer the generated IP to the parti cipating 
companies and support them to reach the commercial phase. Specifically, for the Agro2Circular project Wetsus will 
use it skills, experience and technologies from the research groups: ‘Biopolymers (PHBV) from water’, ‘Advanced 
water treatment’, Resource recovery’ and ‘Desalination’. 
INTEREST IN THE PROJECT 
 
By their participation in A2C project, WETS will increase its knowledge in a key area of its R&D strategy: the water 
treatment and microplastics challenge. The project implementation will also highly widening WETS networks, 
opening opportunities for new collaborations.  
KEY PERSONNEL 
 
 Mr. Erik de Vries  (male). He holds a master degree in biotechnology and a master degree in Business 
administration. He has 13 years of experience in sewage treatment, drinking water production, groundwater 
remediation and resource recovery. As project coordinator and process innovato r he worked for SME’s, local 
governments, utility companies and industry. He currently pursues an academic career and coordinates the tasks 
of WETSUS in EU H2020 project SCALIBUR. His focus is on upscaling of PHBV production technology with 
organic waste/p rimary sewage sludge and secondary sewage sludge as respectively feedstock and functional 
biomass.  
 Dr. Alan Werker (male). He is an environmental engineer with over 30 years of experience in both academic 
and industrial R&D and drove the PHA production te chnology from fundamental laboratory scale to its current 
stage. Alan led a trans -disciplinary team that peaked at 12 research engineers and scientists. Through this work 
he engaged in national and international academic, corporate, and public/private collaborations in basic research, 
thesis supervision, EU Consortium Projects, and in practical business development challenges for renewable 
resource value chains. As well as being the WETSUS ‘Biopolymers from water’ theme leader, Alan Werker is 
co-owner and c onsultant at Promiko AB, a Swedish SME, and an Adjunct Professor, School of Chemical 
Engineering, at the University of Queensland.

RELEVANT PROJECTS OR ACTIVITIES 
 
 The Wetsus research theme ‘Biopolyners from Water’ works on fundamental understanding and upscaling of the 
PHA production technology (Coordination by Alan Werker, currently 2 PhD’s and 1 researcher). The theme is 
sponsored by PAQUES ( http://en.paques.nl ), STOWA ( www.stowa.nl ), and Slibverwerking Noord -Brabant 
(www.snb.nl). The theme strongly believes that PHA production is the future in valorization of arganic waste. 
 H2020 project SCALIBUR (grant nr. 817788) which is currently running, aims to cut urban biowaste and replace 
it with a new production chain of biomaterials, forming a partnership of end users to recover and transform 
biowaste into value added products. Wetsus is responsible for upscaling of the PHA production and recovery from 
fermented organic waste and sewage sludge. A pilot scale PHA accumulation, recovery and evaluation 
infrastructure is being realized.  
 PHARIO was financially subsidised from the Topsector Energy program of the Dutch ministry of Economic 
Affairs (TKI Biobased Economy). It confirmed that surplus full-scale municipal activated sludge can be a robust 
raw material to make biopolymers of predictable and high quality for the bioplastics industry when combined 
with fermented regionally available organic residuals. The techno-economic feasibility for a regional bioplastics 
value chain was demonstrated. 
 EIT RawMaterials upscaling project coordinated by WETSUS on a novel magnetic route for phosphorus and iron 
recovery from sewage sludge (ViviMag). This project is being done in cooperation with TUDELFT (NL), Outotec 
(FI), ICL (IL) and Kemira (FI).  
 H2020 project coordinated by WETSUS on Storage and recovery of renewable electrical energy by reversible salt 
water dissociation (BAoBaB), Grant number: 731187. 
INFRASTRUCTURE AND/OR ANY MAJOR ITEMS OF TECHNICAL EQUIPMENT 
 
Extensive lab and demonstration facilities for numerous water treatment and recource revovery technologies, in -
house and at members of the Water Campus.  
PHA accumulation pilot to produce dried PHA rich biomass from fermented organic waste and surplus activated 
secondary sludge from a municipal waste water treatment plan.  
PHA recovery pilot to extract PHA from PHA rich biomass with green solvents (ATEX proof lab facilities). 
PHA evaluation infrastructure to assess the PHA quality (Rheology, Thermogravimetric analysis, Differential

DESCRIPTION OF THE LEGAL ENTITY  
REGENERA is an SME focused on energy efficiency, renewable energy and the environment. Regenera was 
founded in 2007 in Murcia, Spain. REGENERA is an ESCO with 5 main business lines, offering services, such as 
energy consulting, technical installation, maintenance,  energy services and R&D. We provide holistic solutions to 
increase energy efficiency and flexibility, harvest renewable resources, reduce the environmental impact of industrial, 
residential and commercial activities and boost the competitiveness of our cl ients. Our services include energy 
monitoring, environmental and energy audits, carbon footprint assessment, electricity tariff consulting, design,

installations, preventive, corrective and conductive maintenance and ESCO contracts. Over the years we have worked 
on many different kinds of facilities and projects, and with gained experience and know -how, we are increasingly 
focused in the industrial field.  
We have 6 financed H2020 projects and 2 financed Life project, in addition to nationally and regionally funded 
innovation projects. Our R&D objectives are to digitalize energy processes in order to meet the energy challenges of 
the future and to turn companies’ energy reductions into their main competitive advantage, our focus of innovation 
being demand response and energy flexibility, grid services and smart grids and smart solutions for improving energy 
efficiency and decreasing energy costs, RES integration and management, smart city and mobility solutions, water-
energy nexus, circular economy and industrial symbiosis and other energy solutions and strategies. In addition, we 
provide work with market studies, value network analysis, regulatory and stakeholder analysis and framework, LCA

how in topics, such as smart solutions, Big Data, IoT, modelling, testing, simulation, digital twin, str ucturing of

4.1.12 CEW -CENTRE OF EXPERTISE WATER TREATMENT  
 
PARTNER Nº: 12 (RTO)

LOCATION: Netherlands 
ROLE IN THE PROJECT: PARTNER. 
 
DESCRIPTION OF THE LEGAL ENTITY  
 
CEW is the knowledge and innovation centre when it comes to applied research in the water sector in the Netherlands. 
As a public private partnership between knowledge and research institutions, institutions for vocational education 
(Higher Education), Governmental organisations and entrepreneurs it has the primary goal to develop the knowledge 
of the increasing volume of talent for the International Water Sector and to shorten the valorisation process for the 
innovative industry.  
 
MAIN TASKS IN THE PROJECT 
 
CEW will be involved in WP1, collaborating with WETS in  a strategy for water efficiency across A2C processes 
(T1.3). In WP3 they will collaborate with WETS the near zero liquid discharge water management facility focussed 
on water recovery (reverse osmose, ultrafiltration), micro-plastics removal and organic resource recovery (T3.1), by-
products valorisation of enzymatic process (T3.5.3 . In WP5 they will collaborate with WETS in the PHBV by -
products valorisation (T5.1.2). In WP6 they will be involved in the integration of the developed technology at pilot 
scale in the final A2C demonstrator (T6.1). Moreover, they will be involved in WP8 in communication & 
dissemination activities (T8.2, 8.4, 8.5, 8.6,8.7). 
Related experience: The expertise of CEW relies on their team of professionals with different background that cover 
the whole spectrum of water technology, such as; membrane technologies, chemistry and microbiology, physics and 
modelling. All this knowledge and the know-how, allows to advise and create new concepts and test them reaching 
high TRL in short term.  CEW is participating and coordinated several European projects on water, food and energy 
innovation working closely with SME’s and water utilities to bring innovations to the market. The Water Test 
Network and the VIDA project are examples of it. In these projects, technologies are fostered and tested in a pilot 
scale with TRL ranging from 6 till 9. The expertise of CEW relies on their team of professionals with different 
background that cover the whole spectrum of water technology, such as; membrane technologies, chemistry and 
microbiology, physics and modelling. All this knowledge and the know -how, allows to advise and create new 
concepts and test them reaching high TRL in short term.    
INTEREST IN THE PROJECT   
CEW will broad their knowledge the wastewater characteristics from the plastic waste pre -treatment and/ 
decontamination, and near zero liquid discharge system with high water recovery. CEW will transfer knowledge to 
their associated companies of the wastewater and recycling sectors. Moreover, they will expand its European 
network.

DESCRIPTION OF THE LEGAL ENTITY  
 
CTNC is a private non-profit research association of companies, which is recognized by the Spanish Government 
as Innovation and Technological Centre, Office of Transfer of Research Results and it is declared of Public Use. 
CTNC works in all fields of the food sector: from agriculture to final processed project taking into account containers, 
natural ingredients, valorisation of wastes, environmental impact, etc. CTC has a staff of 32 persons. 
At National and Regional levels CTNC carries out several R&D projects both in the analytical and in the 
technological fields. 
In the analytical field some e xamples are: Suitability of some fruit varieties to be processed, Development of 
molecular methods (PCR and DNA Arrays) for identifying varieties and spices and/or quantifying transgenic DNA 
in food products, Monitoring mycotoxins in food and agricultural products by using latest generation analytical 
techniques, Application of immunochemical techniques for determining antibiotics in honey, Control of pathogens 
in frozen products by using molecular techniques (PCR), Development of new ELISAs for detecting i ntact, 
hydrolysed, toxic prolamins in cereals that are not tolerated by celiac patients, Automated detection of pathogen 
bacteria in food using PCR in real time (quantitative PCR), Development of sensorial analysis in fresh and processed 
fruit and vegetabl es, Nutritional characterization of food products, Pesticide controls in different fruits and 
vegetables, extraction of valuable molecules from agricultural wastes, etc. 
In the technological field, some examples are: Development of functional products in t he meat sector, Study of the 
factors that have an influence on the dissipation of phytosanitary waste during the industrial process of vegetables 
freezing, New active plastic containers for food products. Design of foods with immunizing capacity with an 
artichoke base, development of new food products containing algae, Valorisation of agriculture wastes of broccoli

production, etc. In general CTNC’s expertise in food technology is related with the following technologies: minimally 
processed foods, aseptic processing and packaging, fourth and fifth game products, traditional heat process, freezing 
processes, active containers, by products valorisation, etc., and of course also in everything related with formulation, 
design of processes, shelf life studies, sensorial analysis, extraction of added value molecules from food side streams, 
application to new food products, etc. 
Other CTNC activities are related with technology transfer: ALINNOVA, for fostering innovation in the Spanish 
agrifood sector. (2001/2003),  AGROCSIC, for transferring to the industry the research results of the different

4.1.14 MCT -MARÍN MONTEJANO  AGROTRANSFORMADOS, SA

DESCRIPTION OF THE LEGAL ENTITY  
 
MCT was founded within the Marín Montejano Group in 1986 for the production of juices and drinks in glass and 
brick containers. Throughout the years, the facilities for the packaging of dairy products, wine and derivatives, 
water, gazpacho, jams and other fruit and vegetable preparations, aseptic production lines of fruit preparations 
for industrial use and citrus juice extraction have been extended. 
We have achieved a great development based on the diversification of products, the modernization of facilities and 
the internationalization of markets but without losing the familiar character that allows an agile management and a 
complete implication of the property in all the projects. 
We currently have a presence in over 40 countries, both with our own brands and with private labels and industrial 
semi-finished products. 
We also work as co-packers for different companies in the food sector, contributing our experience and knowledge 
to the needs of these clients. 
We cover the complete manufacturing process in our own facilities; design, development, manufacturing, storage, 
labelling and shipping. 
✓ Commitment to Quality and Safety : Every year we are successfully audited to maintain our IFS 
certification and operate under an ISO 9001 management system, as well as having our customers' own 
systems accreditations. 
✓ Social and Environmental Commitment: We have implemented a CSR (Corporate Social Responsibility) 
system and are members of Sedex. We have received various awards such as the Commitment to Sustainable 
Development in the Region of Murcia and we are certified packers of organic products. 
✓ Commitment to R&D. In recent years we have been making a major effort to develop and market new 
products in the line of organic and healthy products. Likewise, we have achieved important improvements 
in the production processes with a view to improving the quality, s ustainability and competitiveness of our 
products.

DESCRIPTION OF THE LEGAL ENTITY  
 
Laboratorios Almond S.L.  was created in 1995 with the idea of manufacturing food supplements and 100% 
vegetable food preparations . The company offers a wide range of products 100% vegetable and free of most 
allergens, so they are suitable for people with allergies to milk protein and / or egg, lactose intolerances and / or 
gluten. The commercialization of the products is done under the brand NATURGREEN. 
 
Among its range of products are oils and dressings, soups, sugars, cereals, desserts, beverage all made with organic 
certification and non -dairy ingredients. Company has seven production lines: Bio oils, Bio syrups, Bio powder 
products, Bio vegetable desse rts and creams, fermented non-dairy desserts, Packaging in doy pack format of 
sweeteners and Packaging in doy pack format of dry food. 
 
 

Section 4,5,6-page 34

INTEREST IN THE PROJECT

use of their own waste and by-products as raw materials.  Promotion of a new business line in the circular economy.

4.1.16 PROEX -PROEXPORT  
 
• PARTNER Nº: 16 (NPO) 
• WEBSITE: www.proexport.es 
• SHORTNAME: PROEX

DESCRIPTION OF THE LEGAL ENTITY  
 
 
PROEXPORT, the Association of Producers-Exporters of Fruits and Vegetables in the Region of Murcia, 
defend the interests of the industry and fighting since 1975 to get the best results for our partners. Proexport 
companies are industry leaders in a 20% of moves that national exports of fruits and vegetables. 
 
PROEXPORT partners (> 50) employ more than 28,000 directly workers, selling a million tons of nearly various 
fruits and vegetables. In addition, we concentrate more than 70% of total regional production and export of these 
products, boosting the regional economy directly. An average of 1,2 million T ons of vegetables and fruits are 
exported each year by partners of Proexport and more than 60 countries consume products from our partners. They 
are a benchmark in quality and food safety, technological development, internationalization and CSR.  
 
Proexport is committed to the environment and collaborate in eco-friendly projects, improv ing the 
competitiveness  of horticultural  farms  in the Murcia  region   
PROEXPORT provides its members with services such as technical research, environmental programmes, marketing 
actions, phytosanitary measures, innovation plans and it talks on its members’ behalf in regional, national and 
European institutions. 
The Technical Department is in charge of the environmental, research and innovation, and phytosanitary measures 
to be adopted by the growers in order to improve their agricultural productions, organizational systems, 
environmental sustainability and any other issue needed or helpful to its members. 
 
MAIN TASKS IN THE PROJECT 
 
PROEX will be  involved in WP1 defining the needs and characteristics that new agricultural films and food 
packaging should display to be used (T1.1), the requirements the residues management plan must meet and the basis 
to the setting-up plan (T1.4). In WP5, they will validate the new agricultural films compared to conventional films 
in horticultural soils (T5.4.2).   
Proexport will be one of the providers of the samples for the project developments (vegetable waste-WP2 and 
agricultural films-WP3) to be turned into new bioplastics compounds and will test the new packaging materials. 
 
PROEX will also collaborate on public engagement at regional levels ( T7.1), regional socioeconomic assessment 
(data collection on T.4), the elaboration of the A2C Circular economy action plan (within T7.5) as well as and on 
cross fertilization actions for multidimensional model validation (T7.7). 
PROEX will also participate on WP8: A2C Outreach, by being mainly involved in awareness and engagement 
actions (T8.3)  as well on T8.6 (knowledge transfer). 
 
Related experience: As fruit and vegetable growers and packers, Proexport and its members have a vast knowledge 
in the agrifood sector and are extensive users of agricultural films and packaging materials, such as multilayer 
plastics, so replacing fossil-based plastics with new agri-food debris-based plastics would mean a giant step towards 
circular economy. 
 
INTEREST IN THE PROJECT 
 
In joining this project, PROEX expects the producers and packers’ needs will be met regarding the systemic solution 
in the agrifood sector to be set up, moreover when the source of the new material will be the very plant debris and 
food waste currently pose a challenge.  PROEX will share the acquire d knowledge with their associated agrifood 
companies. They will enlarge their European networking.

DESCRIPTION OF THE LEGAL ENTITY  
 
DMC Research Center SL is a technological-based entity with headquarters in Alhendín (Granada). The company 
was created in 2005 to create a specific R&D Department of the linked company DOMCA. DMC Research belongs 
to DMC business group constituted by DOMCA Spain and DMC Researc h Center SL. The group has a factory in 
Argentina (DOMCA Argentina), from where the products are distributed to America. Recently, the company has 
started to operate in Chile, with special focus on the aquaculture sector.  

Section 4,5,6-page 37 
 
The team of DMC is composed of hi ghly qualified professionals in Microbiology, Chemistry, Food Science and 
Technology among others. DMC Research has one of the leading research groups in Andalusia, having the greatest 
research activity in biotechnological applications. The research lines are very diverse and range from the selection 
of microorganisms and plant extracts with application for human and animal nutrition to the development of new 
food preservation technologies based on edible coatings, active packaging or air-sanitation. 
Currently, DMC Research Center is working in the following lines: 
 
1.- Obtaining new natural -based compounds (from plants and microorganisms) with technological and functional 
properties. 
2.- Development of new products against emerging pathogens. 
3.- Sanitation processes for the food industry. 
4.- Natural systems in post-harvest treatments and biological pest control. 
5.- Product development for new packaging methods. 
6.- Studies of stabilization and controlled release of active ingredients. 
7.- Use of by-products from the agri-food industry. 
8.- Development of functional ingredients for animal feed. 
9.- New functional ingredients from plant extracts intended for human nutrition. 
 
DMC Research Center collaborates with several Universities and Technological Centers, both from Spain and other 
European countries. The entity has collaboration agreements with different departments of the University of Granada, 
Sevilla or Murcia. As a result of these collaborations, the company has several patents, know-how transfer agreements 
and significant scientific publications. 
MAIN TASKS IN THE PROJECT 
 
DMC will be involved in WP1, collaborating in the definition of the new food, nutraceutics formulations (T1.1), 
collaborating in the implementation of methodology for new formulations with extracts from agri-food wastes (T1.2). 
In WP2, they will develop in collaboration with CTNC and SSICA the hybrid route of green solvents+enzymatic 
hydrolisis+ microwave assisted extraction (T2.2), the y will collaborate in the purification and stabilisation of the 
extracts (T2.3) and will lead the evaluation of the extractions (T2.4). In WP4, they will be involved in the formulation 
of new food and nutraceuticals formulations at small scale using the extracts (T4.1), and they will implement at pilot 
scale at their facilities the green solvents+enzymatic hydrolisis+ microwave assisted extraction route (T4.2). In WP6, 
they will be end users validating the bioactive extracts in a real environment by develop ment of new food & 
nutraceuticals formulations (T6.2). Moreover, they will be involved in WP8 in communication & dissemination 
activities (T8.2, 8.4, 8.5, 8.6,8.7). 
Related experience : DMC has a wide expertise in the implementation of natural product extraction methods, 
especially bioactive compounds extracted from allium species. DMC has been supporting the linked company 
DOMCA in developing high added value additives for food, nutraceuticals, feed and agriculture as well as 
characterizing the extracts and their properties (antioxidant, antimicrobial, etc.) with the most advanced technologies 
INTEREST IN THE PROJECT 
 
The A2C project is fully aligned with the R&D priority lines of DMC. In fact, the activities included in the project 
will allow us to continue improving our capabilities with the aim to offer the best support and include the waste reuse 
as a desired objective in our extraction processes. New circular business. New products based on natural bioactives 
from agrifood wastes. Increasing their comtetitiveness.

markets. To this end, we are certified by the Organic Agriculture Council of the Region of Murcia, n: ES-ECO-024-

4.1.2 0 SSICA - EXPERIMENTAL STATION FOR THE FOOD PRESERVATION INDUSTRY  
 
PARTNER Nº: 20 (RTO) 
WEBSITE: www.ssica.it  
SHORTNAME: SSICA 
LOCATION: Italy 
ROLE IN THE PROJECT: PARTNER.  
 
DESCRIPTION OF THE LEGAL ENTITY  
 
Since 1922, The Experimental Station for the Food Preserving Industry (SSICA),  operating through its 
headquarters in Parma and the section of Angri (Salerno), has been promoting the scientific and technical progress 
of the Italian food-preserving industry for the sectors of packaging, fruits, vegetables, meat and fish products through 
activities of research, consultancy, training and dissemination of information . In the production chain of the 
agrifood sector SSICA activity supplies suitable solutions to the food preserving industry in terms of product and 
process safety, innovation,  technology, methodology and use of raw materials. Applied research and pilot -scale 
experimental tests are carried out in SSICA chemical, instrumental, technological and microbiological laboratories. 
Thanks to its specialized staff and cutting -edge laboratories, SSICA is one of the most important applied research 
bodies in the preserved food sector in Europe and in the world and takes part in national and international research 
projects. The Institute includes area specific to different product sectors, as well as departments and laboratories in 
charge of more general activities; with its skilled staff and updated equipment it is able to experiment with new 
products, new processing and preservation procedures, also analysing their economic and social impact.  In 2016 
SSICA has become a national foundation for international research. 
 
  
 

Section 4,5,6-page 42 
 
MAIN TASKS IN THE PROJECT 
 
SSICA will be involved in WP2, where they will collaborate in the agri-food waste classification and conditioning 
(T2.1), they will carry out R&D in collaboration with CTNC in the green hybrid extraction routes (T2.2), they will 
lead the purification and stabilisation of the extracts (T2.3) and in the evaluation of the extractions (T2.4). In WP4, 
they will be involved in the formulation of new food and nutraceuticals formulations at small scale using the extracts 
(T4.1), and they will assist to MKSI & DMC in the implemention at pilot scale of the green solvents+enzymatic 
hydrolisis+microwave assisted extraction route (T4.2). In WP6, they will be in the integration of the technologies at 
pilot scale (T6.2). Moreover, they will be involved in WP8 in communication & dissemination activities (T8.2, 8.4, 
8.5, 8.6,8.7). 
 
Related experience: SSICA’s Sensory & Consumer Area has been dealing for years with the extraction of bio -
functional molecules from the waste of industrial processing of various plant species (apple, tomato, apricot, onions, 
strawberries, green beans, banana, kiwi, pear, to mato seeds, peas) and the subsequent optimization marketing & 
consumer based of food products formulas with these added substances. In particular, they have experience in the 
extraction, purification & stabilisation of functional substances (carotenoids, phytosterols) and also several phenolic 
compounds (naringenin, kaempferol, rutin, chorogenic acid, quercetin, quercetin 3 -O-β-glucoside, rhamnetin, 
miricetin, caffeic acid, vanillic acid, cumaric acid, ferulic acid, acido ellagic acid, gallic acid) have also been extracted 
from industrial processing waste. The undertaken studies were aimed at enhancing the waste from the food industry 
with a view to developing new functional ingredients and represent a possible solution linked to the onerous problem 
of the disposal of industrial processing waste; the transformation of the latter into added value ingredients on the one 
hand reduces the environmental impact associated with their disposal and, on the other, creates an economically 
significant commodity resource. 
 
INTEREST IN THE PROJECT 
 
By its participation in the A2C project, SSICA will broad its knowledge and experience in extraction, and stabilisation 
of bioactives from agrifood wastes, and in optimizing the ingredient composition of traditional as well as novel foods 
according to technological processes and in determining the driving factors (drivers) for the overall satisfaction of 
different consumer market segments. Moreover, they will promote the replication to show the innovation in the sector 
and will create new lines for training in the agrifood sector. 
 
KEY PERSONNEL 
 
 Prof. Sebastiano Porretta (male). Sebastiano Porretta is a senior researcher of the Italian Ministry of Economic

for research in the study of product development and quality. His original approach to studying t he interactions

SSICA has full equipped facilities including the following equipment: 
 
- pilot multi-functional lines, including mixer, colloid mill, cutter, homogenization units, decanter centrifuge 
(solid/liquid horizontal separation), centrifuge (liquid/liquid separation), air dryer, close type microwa ve pilot

(only for aqueous samples) and laboratory scale freeze dryer.

triple quadrupole, UPLC HRMS orbitrap. 
- Sensory Analysis Laboratory, operating in accordance with ISO 8589 
- Encapsulator B-390 Bϋchi, to encapsulate various materials into a polymeric matrix using vibrating technology 
(prilling) to form beads and capsules with particle diameters between 80 µm and 4000 µm. The encapsulator is 
provided with a concentric nozzle system for creating core-shell capsules. 
 
In the project will collaborate the following sections: 
- The Factory section deals with research, projects and support to companies on plants and engineering issues, 
with particular regard to technology, process and product innovation, process validation (heat penetration 
during sterilization and pasteurization) and  plant validation (retorts and other types of sterilizers and 
pasteurizers) for the heat treatment of food.  
- The Chemical Safety section offers services and research activities mainly dealing with chemical food risks, 
in particular relating to contamination from pesticide residues, leaching from materials in contact with food, 
use of improper additives and, in general, intentional or unintentional contaminants.  
- The Consumer Science section  deals with the design and development of new products or the updati ng of 
existing ones will carry out a significant part of the project activity. The focus is mainly on the quality of food 
Section 4,5,6-page 44 
 
and the evaluation of compositional characteristics, identifying relationships between chemical, physical and 
sensory and market markers. Within the Department, the Sensory Analysis and Consumer Science Laboratory 
is operating in accordance with ISO 8589. 
- The Microbiology section. The main task of the section is to ensure the stability and the microbiological safety 
of food products thro ugh a series of activities that involve implementation of research projects on specific 
topics, direct assistance to companies through analysis and consultancy services, planning of training courses 
for food industry technicians. 
- The Microbiology area collaborates with the technological section so as to address the various issues with an 
integrated approach.

 INVESTSOCIAL (AVI, INNTAL21/18/014). Impact Investment – a novel outcome -based financing 
mechanism to promote innovation and social well-being. Impact investments are those investments that direct 
capital towards projects with social and/or environmental impact. The double search for profitability and social 
/ environmental impact is what differentiates impact investments from other types of investments. Despite the 
fact that impact investment is gaining increasing attention and it has now become a relevant issue even on the 
EU public agenda, there is still much confusion about this emerging market. The application of such investment 
schemes is complicated and requires specific feasibility analysis.  This research focuses on the  study of one of 
these instruments, the Social Impact Bond,  and its potential application  for the  finance of local or regional 
interventions for energy poverty.  Duration: from 2018 -02-01 to 2020 -12-31, ongoing 
project. Website: http://kveloce.com/en/formacion/recursos/

tackling energy poverty. WELLBASED will design, implement and evaluate a comprehensive urban 
programme to reduce energy poverty and their effects on the citizens health and well being, built on evidence -
based approaches in 7 different pilot cities, representing different urban realities but also a diverse range of 
welfare and healthcare models.  KVC is in charge of  developing,  together  with project  partners,  the  urban

4.1.22 UVEG -POLIBIENESTAR  
 
PARTNER Nº: 22 (UNIVERSITY)

ROLE IN THE PROJECT: PARTNER. 
 
DESCRIPTION OF THE LEGAL ENTITY  
The Universitat de València (UVEG) was founded in 1499 and, initially, was dedicated to the study of Medicine, 
Humanities, Theology and Law. Nowadays, it has become a modern European university opened to almost every 
branch of knowledge. Given the wide ran ge of studies offered as well as its humanistic dimension, the Universitat 
de València is now one of the largest, oldest, and most diverse universities in Spain. The University has 45,800 
degree and 8,600 postgraduate students. On our campuses (Blasco Ibañ ez, Burjassot-Paterna and Els Tarongers), 
over 3,300 teachers and researchers, who make up 90 departments, 17 institutes and other research units, carry out 
their work, aided by over 1,700 administration and service staff. Its libraries hold almost 1,5 mil lion books, are 
subscribed to more than 26,000 journals, and provide 4,300 reading places for its almost 60,000 users. Along with 
the human resources, the magnitude of its facilities and the available up -to-date instrumental equipment guarantee 
the quality of a vast scientific and technologic offer to the service of society.   
The UVEG is recognized as one of the most outstanding Spanish universities in both national and international 
rankings. It produces 63% of the indexed references of all Valencian univ ersities and ranks third among Spanish 
universities in indexed scientific production. More than 300 PhD theses are presented every year in the framework 
of 110 PhD programs, 31 of which have obtained the special Quality Award given by the Spanish Education  
Ministry. At last, its increasing research budget, over € 52 million, is an indicator of the scientific and technological 
capabilities of the UVEG.  The UVEG has experience in the development and management of more than 150 
European Projects under the fol lowing frameworks: the RTD European (I to VII) Framework Programmes, 
HORIZON 2020, Lifelong Learning Programme (Erasmus, Socrates, Leonardo) and Erasmus+, acting both as a 
coordinator and partner institution.    
In particular, Polibienestar Research Institute which belongs to UVEG, is composed by an interdisciplinary team 
with 38 senior and 18 junior researchers with national and European experience from nine different departments 
from the UVEG and six associated units from the Universities: Castellón, Murc ia, Castilla La Mancha, Castilla y 
León, Extremadura, and Politécnica de Madrid. The staff of Polibienestar is composed by researchers from different 
backgrounds working together to study health and social phenomena, including experts on medicine, psycholo gy, 
sociology, political science, social work, economy, law, education engineering, and architecture. This allows to carry 
out interdisciplinary research, innovation and social technology, technical advice, and training in the fields of health 
and social p olicies. Polibienestar also advises the Administration and private entities in the design, planning and 
implementation of health and social policies and services. To date, Polibienestar has participated and coordinated 
more than 40 R&D projects funded by Spanish Ministries and European programmes like the 6th and 7th Framework 
Programmes, the II and III Health Programmes, the AAL Programme, the Daphne III Programme, the Progress 
Programme, the ENPI CBCMED, the Youth in Action Programme, the Life Long Learni ng Programme, H2020, 
among others.    
Additionally, Polibienestar presents a broad experience in cooperation and participation in European networks due 
to its active role in European research and policy design. Among others, Polibienestar works together with CORAL– 
Community of Regions for Assisted Living and ENSA. Furthermore, Polibienestar participates actively in two 
Action Groups of the European Innovation Partnership on Active and Healthy Ageing (EIP on AHA) promoted by 
the European Commission: B3 Capa city building and replicability of successful integrated care systems based on 
innovative tools and services and D4 Innovation for age friendly buildings, cities and environments.   
MAIN TASKS IN THE PROJECT 
UVEG will participate in the project providing a  horizontal perspective of SSH and RRI content to the project 
implementation. UVEG will lead the construction of the multidimensional model for A2C systemic solution  
adoption, replication and replication (T7.5) with a special focus on delivering policy&regulatory recommendations 
as well as on constructing the A2C circular governance model while it will actively participate along the WP7 ,

building (T8.6)

INTEREST IN THE PROJECT  
Polibienestar has strong leadership position and capacity to carry out number of activities related to the topic ID LC-
GD-3-2-2020, such as (a) policy recommendations and guidelines to advice policy makers in different topics, 
especially in the promotion of initiatives addressed to foster sustainable behaviors among citizens (circular economy) 
and wellbeing; (b) use of different assessment tools to measure the change of behaviors and the impact at social and 
health dimensions of citizens; (c) identification, analysis and evaluation of policies, programmes and interventions, 
including model definition and replication analysis; (d) detection, design and assessment of good practices and 
initiatives in the field; (e ) promote the participation of end -users, especially vulnerable groups, in the project 
activities; (f) implementing specific training activities.

RELEVANT PROJECTS OR ACTIVITIES 
 
 SCIROCCO: Scaling Integrated Care in Context. Co-funded by the Health Programme of the European Union 
(ref.: 710033). Main researcher in UVEG: Jorge Garcés. Duration: 32 months. The project provided a validated 
and tested self-assessment tool to facilitate scaling up and successful transfer of good practices in integrated care 
through European regions. This tool is now been supported by the project SIROCCO Exchange funded by the 
same programme in which Polibienestar also participates. 
 CONCISE: Communication role on perception and beliefs of EU  citizens about science (H2020 SWAFS; 
European Commission).  Main researcher in UVEG: Carolina Moreno. Duration: 2018 -2021. CONCISE aims 
to generate a European -wide debate on science communication, involving a wide array of stakeholders, from 
media outlets to policy makers, from scientists to business companies, from science communicators to civil 
society organisations. 
 VALUECARE - Value-based methodology for integrated care supported by ICT. Funded under the Horizon 
2020 Programme of the EC (ref.: 875215). Main researcher in UVEG: Jorge Garcés. Duration: 2019-2023. The 
project delivers efficient outcome -based integrated (health and social) care to older people facing cognitive 
impairment, frailty and multiple chronic health conditions in order to improve th eir quality of life (and of their 
families) as well as the sustainability of the health and social care systems in Europe. 
 EURIPHI - European wide Innovation Procurement in Health and Care. Funded under the Horizon 2020 
Programme of the EC (ref.: 825922). Main researcher in UVEG: Jorge Garcés. Duration: 2019 -2020. This a 
CSA project aimed at developing a model of “Innovative Public Procurement” (PPI) across borders fostering 
acceleration in a change in procurement practices leading to a value-based approach resulting in most economic 
advantageous tendering.   
 Dinamising Circular Economy in the Innovation System in Valencia region  (funded by the regional 
government). Main researcher in UVEG: Jorge Garcés. Duration: 2018. The project fostered and reinforced the 
implementation of the circular economy initiatives among the universities and research institutes in the Valencia 
region.

4.1.23 CJM -FUNDACIÓN CAJAMAR  
PARTNER Nº: 23 (NGO) 
WEBSITE: www.fundacioncajamar.es  
SHORTNAME: CJM 
LOCATION: SPAIN 
ROLE IN THE PROJECT: PARTNER 
 
DESCRIPTION OF THE LEGAL ENTITY  
 
Fundación Cajamar is a Spanish non-profit foundation created by Cajamar credit cooperative bank in 2006 with the 
aim of ‘generating knowledge and disseminating it to the whole society’.  
 

Section 4,5,6-page 50 
 
Particularly, Fundación Cajamar encompasses three action lines: Financing lines and support to the agrifood sector, 
training programmes and dissemination actions, research activities related to the agrifood sector 
Financial support to the agrifood sector:  Fundacion Cajamar is committed with the agrifood sector, supporting 
the financing needs and offering financial solution through special financial lines tailored to each specific needs 
(some of them trough rural banks that are part of the Cajamar Cooperative Group) as well as offering a supporting 
service on financial assessment. Some of the financing lines are:  
 Agricultural / Livestock Campaign Loan to cover up to 100% of the expenses derived from your activity. 
Quickly granted and with preferential interest rates. 
 Campaign Loans for Cooperatives and Societies to meet the needs and unforeseen events that arise during 
the campaign. 
 Credit Account to cover the liquidity needs produced by the development of activities in the primary sector 
in a comfortable way, as a current account. 
 Agrofuerte credit that is available through the businesses adhered to this system, being able to choose the 
form of payment in each purchase. Allowing to adjust payments to the collection cycles of your farm. 
Knowledge transfer and dissemination actions: Cajamar Agrifood traini ng is another step in the search for 
synergies with the agri -food sector, and includes specific training actions designed with the aim of promoting 
innovation and competitiveness of the business throughout the entire agrifood value chain. 
Training and knowledge are the engines that contribute to innovation in the agrifood sector, promoting the economic, 
social and environmental sustainability of the sector, based on permanent contact with the rest of the agents in the 
value chain and through the incorporation of technology, professional training and sustainable practices. 
For this reason, we periodically organize transfer activities (conferences, seminars, workshops) and training courses 
for directors and managers of agrifood companies, as well as courses for young people in order for them to join the 
agrifood sector and develop their professional activity in it. 
Research activities: The research activity is carried out in its research centre located at the Southeast of Spain in the 
middle of the highest conc entration of greenhouses in Europe. This centre has been doing experimentation on 
greenhouse horticulture from its creation by Cajamar in 1975. The research activity is focused on the development 
of new technologies for the bioeconomy and the search of alt ernative productions for Mediterranean greenhouses, 
keeping always in mind the sustainability of the greenhouse system, both in terms of resources (water, nutrients, 
energy, etc.), waste management, revaluation of by-products of the agricultural sector. The research team has specific 
skills on improving water use and irrigation scheduling in horticultural greenhouse crops, biological pest control, 
fertigation management, cultivation techniques, greenhouse technology, bioeconomy and circular agricultural. 
 
The research activity is divided into four departments: Agri -Sustainability, Greenhouse Technology, Food and 
Health, and Bio-Economy. Furthermore, there is a horizontal Dissemination department. A constant communication 
with the different stakeholders of th e greenhouse industry, from growers and technical advisors (through the 
cooperatives) to greenhouse-related technology manufacturers, as well as with other research centres is promoted. 
Dissemination activity is a core objective and is carried out through the publication of technical documents (which 
are free -available in the following webpage: http://www.publicacionescajamar.es/), the organization of transfer 
activities across the country (more than 100 per year with almost 8,000 attendants), and attending  the visits to the 
centre (almost 4,000 visitors). 
 
MAIN TASKS IN THE PROJECT 
CJM will support UB in the development the Circular Economy business models (T6.4) focusing on the study of the 
specific financing needs of each partner arising from the CEBMs. Thus, CJM will identify the financing need of 
each generated business model related to the specific partner involved and will explore which private fund will better 
support each CEBMs. Moreover, CJM will actively participate in 7.1 on public engagement actions and in 7.5.3 
helping to delivering the financing recommendations for CEBMs adoption also at EU levels.  CJM will also 
participate in A2C Outreach activities, especially on actions for knowledge transfer and capacity building (T8.6)  
INTEREST IN THE PROJECT 
The implementation of this project and its results will provide CJM a valuable knowledge and understanding about  
the circular economy related needs which will enable to better adjust their financial instruments for the agrifood 
sector fostering their transition towards circular economy

4.1.25 UNE-ASOCIACIÓN ESPAÑOLA DE NORMALIZACIÓN  
PARTNER Nº: 25 (NPO) 
WEBSITE: https://www.en.une.org/ 
SHORTNAME: UNE  
LOCATION: Spain 
ROLE IN THE PROJECT: PARTNER 
 
DESCRIPTION OF THE LEGAL ENTITY  
The Spanish Association for Standardization (UNE) is legally designated as the National Standardization Body of 
Spain. It is the national representative and member of the European (CEN/CENELEC), International (ISO/IEC) and 
Panamerican (COPANT) Organizations for Standardization, and member of the European Tel ecommunications 
Standards Institute (ETSI). More than 32.000 standards in catalogue, 200 national technical committees and 150 
responsibilities (chairpersons, secretariats, convenors) in international standardization committees are a sample of 
the experience developed as national standards body during more than 30 years. Formally, it is a non -profitmaking, 
private, independent and multisectoral organisation, recognised at national, European and international level. 
Through the development of technical stand ards UNE helps to improve the quality and competitiveness of 
companies, products and services. 
MAIN TASKS IN THE PROJECT 
Advising, managing and developing all the activities related with standardization, carried out within WP8 framework, 
at tasks T8.8.1: Analysis of the applicable standardization landscape  (closely interrelated and in collaboration 
with T1.2: A2C methodologi es) and Task T8.8.2: Contribution to the ongoing and future standardization 
developments (closely interrelated and in collaboration with 7.5.2.:Regulatory, standardization and political 
relevant factors at European level.) 

Section 4,5,6-page 54 
 
The European Standardization Organizations CEN and CENELEC do not participate directly in research and 
innovation projects, delegating this participation to their national members. 
INTEREST IN THE PROJECT 
Representing the European standardization organizations CEN and CENELEC, UNE is participating in many 
research and innovation projects (Horizon 2020, FP7, Life+, CIP etc., see examples here) to support and manage the 
integration of standardization activities, increasing impact by fostering the dissemination of the results to the relevant 
European stakeholders and facilitating their market uptake. UNE is also an active member of the CEN -CENELEC 
Strategic Group ‘STAIR’ (STAndardization, Innovation and Research), which develops guidelines for the practical 
integration of these three activities and responsible for the Standards+Innovation initiative.

AGRO is a meeting point for business-oriented organizations which come together to work on common solutions for 
developing cooperation projects in their field of expertise, interest or influence. Agrofood is comprised of important 
institutions and firms in the agrofood industry, providing solutions to market needs through business cooperation and 
collaboration, and presenting valuable solutions and turnkey projects by working together because "true knowledge 
is a collective enterprise". 
AGRO offers solutions in product innovation, int ernationalization, implementation of new processes and 
environmental efficiency. The goal of Agrofood is to help entrepreneurs overcome strategic challenges and develop 
competitive solutions.

INTEREST IN THE PROJECT

4.1.27 EURA - ASSOCIATION EUROPÉENNE DES AGENCES DE DÉVELOPPEMENT  
 
PARTNER Nº: 27 (NPO) 
WEBSITE: http://www.eurada.org/ 
SHORTNAME: EURA  
LOCATION: Belgium 
ROLE IN THE PROJECT: PARTNER 
 
DESCRIPTION OF THE LEGAL ENTITY  
The European Association of Development Agencies (EURADA) was established in 1992 to support policy learning 
in regional development agencies. A Development Agency is an operational structure created by local or regional 
public entities to effectively support SME competitiveness in their territory. Development agencies identify sectoral 
or general development problems, choose a range of opportunities for their solution, and promote projects that can 
maximize solutions. 
The core activities of EURADA are directed towards sharing good practices to increase the impact of the 
development agencies and work on common projects, in special those dedicated to entrepreneurship, social 
innovation and support for SMEs. In practice, EURADA is a network of practitioners sharing their experiences and 
making common projects. To help them to contact with the other members of the network, EURADA organises 
several conferences, matchmaking events and workshops every year to foster the exchang e of experiences and the 
design of new projects.   
EURADA has established a framework of continuous dialogue with the European Commission and other EU 
Institutions to launch new policy to foster economic growth. In the framework of its dialogue, EURADA participates 
in several committees of the EU, like the Network of SME Envoys (E02666), Consultative and supportive Group for 
the Enterprise Europe Network (E02814), the experts’ group for the follow-up of the Small Business Act, the mirror 
group for smart specialisation or the expert group for the Structured Dialogue of ESI Funds (E03226).   
 
MAIN TASKS IN THE PROJECT 
EURA will lead networking and clustering activities on T8.5 as well as will collaborate along the WP8, specially 
on T8.6 actions for knowledge transfer and capacity bulging.  
EURA will actively participate on Public engagement actions at European levels ( T7.1), and on T7.5: Analysis of 
European policies and financi al instruments related to the circular economy as well as collaborating on delivering 
recommendations fostering the circular economy. At this respect, EURA will be especially in charge on exploring 
Public procurement as well as on recommendations to foster it. 
EURA will also collaborate on the analysis of the A2C circular governance model as well as on the elaboration of 
the A2C multidimensional model and its self-assessment tools and its validation. 
 
INTEREST IN THE PROJECT 
As professional association of r egional economic practitioners, EURADA is committed to facilitate the replication 
of the outcomes of the project and in general to facilitate the outreach, communication, dissemination, and 
exploitation of results (WP9). The non-profit association has proven expertise in this area being the responsible for 
communication and dissemination in two ongoing H2020 projects (TeRRItoria and TetRRIs) and two Interreg Europe 
projects (SocialSeeds and Scaleup). Through its large network of local and regional economic practitioners, 
EURADA will act as an umbrella association reaching relevant stakeholders and disseminating the outputs of the 
project among them.

4.1.28 UB - UNIVERSITA COMMERCIALE LUIGI BOCCONI  
 
PARTNER Nº: 28 (RTO) 
WEBSITE: www.unibocconi.it; www.green.unibocconi.it 
SHORTNAME: UB 
LOCATION: Italy 
ROLE IN THE PROJECT: PARTNER 
 
 
DESCRIPTION OF THE LEGAL ENTITY  
Established in 1902, Università Bocconi is a university of international standing in business, economics and law. Its 
research projects are funded by national and supranational institutions.  
Università Bocconi has participated in more than 100 projects funded by the European Union and other international 
and national donors. At present, it is involved (as coordinator or partner) in about 60 Socio-Economic Sciences and 
Health projects funded by the European Union and other international and national donors,  including 6 Starting 
Grants, 2 Consolidator Grants, 4 Advanced Grants of the European Research Council and 2 Marie Curie projects. 
Having hosted 18 grants funded by the ERC, Bocconi ranks 1st in Europe in the panel SH1 “Individual, Institutions 
and Markets: Economics, Finance and Management”. GREEN – Geography, Resources, Environment, Energy and 
Networks is the research centre which co-ordinates and conducts applied research in the following fields:  
• Energy economics, focusing on energy markets as well as on natural resources;  
• Environmental economics, focusing on environmental and climate policy, analysis and evaluation; circular 
economy. 
• Economics of public utilities focusing on energy, water and waste services.  
GREEN Bocconi (UB) is and has been involved in several national and European projects, both as coordinator and 
as partner (namely European projects funded on Horizon 2020, Intelligent Energy Europe, LIFE+, Alpine Space, 
MED). UB is specialized in providing support to policy elaboration, moni toring and evaluation through the 
application of several methodologies, including cost-benefit analysis, evaluation of externalities, economic modelling 
and scenario development.  
The main research areas regard multi -level policies for climate (mitigation,  adaptation), GHG reduction planning, 
GHG monitoring, resource efficiency, circularity, energy efficiency, environment and competitiveness, regulatory, 
economic and voluntary instruments for the environment, smart and low carbon cities, climate finance, environmental 
information and public participation. Thanks to the expertise of its research team UB adopts a multidisciplinary 
approach.  
UB has working relations with several research organizations. It is member of the Sustainable Development Solutions 
Network (SDSN), a global initiative launched by the United Nations involving academia, civil society, and the private 
sector to support sustainable development problem solving. It is an associated member of the Urban Europe Research 
Alliance (UERA). It is also  partner of: UN -HABITAT CPI initiative and UNEP’s GI -REC initiative on Global 
Resource Efficient Cities. 
MAIN TASKS IN THE PROJECT 
UB will be responsible for the identification of circular business models in the agri -food sector with a special 
focus on the evaluation of local and territorial impacts , and will support partners in business models 
identification and analysis, and integrates natural capital accounting within the circular business models  
(T6.4). UB will be also involved in the financing analysis for the A2C CEBMs and it will be involved together with 
specialised partners in the study of financing schemes framework (T7.5), delivering recommendations for financing 
schemes fostering circular solutions and its dissemination/training related activities (T8.7). UB will also provide data 
for the evaluation and monitoring of the A2C cluster progress towards circularity and to benchmark A2C circular 
solution (7.2). UB will collaborate in the socioeconomic analysis (7.3) as well as support to replication partners on 
T7.7 on CEBMs related issues and participate in the validation of the A2C multidimensional model  for adoption, 
replication and scalability (T7.6)  
INTEREST IN THE PROJECT 
UB has participated in several research projects on circular economy approaches in different sectors, and circular 
economy is one of the main work areas of GEO – green economy observatory – a think -tank launched by UB 
involving more than 50 companies and o rganizations ( http://www.geo.unibocconi.it/ ). UB is also in charge of 
business model analysis and circular economy and evaluation in ongoing Horizon 2020 projects involving cities 

Section 4,5,6-page 60 
 
(UrbanGreenUP and MAtchUP) and CINDERELA project, supporting and guiding the construction sector towards 
circular economy.

4.1.29 VTT -VTT TECHNICAL RESEARCH CENTRE OF FINLAND LTD  
 
PARTNER Nº: 29 (RTO) 
WEBSITE: https://www.vttresearch.com 
SHORTNAME: VTT 
LOCATION: Finland 
ROLE IN THE PROJECT: PARTNER 
 
DESCRIPTION OF THE LEGAL ENTITY  
 
VTT Technical Research Centre of Finland Ltd is a state owned and controlled non-profit limited liability company 
established by law and operating under the ownership steering of the Finnish Ministry of Employment and the 
Economy. VTT is an RTO whose activities are focused on three areas: Knowledge intensive products and services, 
Smart industry and energy systems, and Solutions for natural resources and environment. VTT is impact-driven and 
takes advantage from its wide multitechnological knowledge base to  strengthen Finnish and European industrial 
competitiveness.  
VTT has a staff of 2054, net turnover in 2018 was 159,7M€ and other operational incomes were 81,2M€. Over the 
years, VTT has gained vast experience from participation and coordination of numerous European projects including 
R&D Framework Programme projects and other thematic frameworks and programmes. VTT is ranked among the 
leading European RTOs. In December 2017, VTT has been recognised with the “HR Excellence in Research” award 
by the European Commission.  
MAIN TASKS IN THE PROJECT 
VTT will lead the Task 7.3: Environmental assessment, LCA and A2C circularity monitoring, identifying, 
analyzing and addressing environmental impacts and externalities through and LCA methodology, providing the 
partner technology developers a valuable knowledge about their processes impact and how to address and minimize 
them within the project implementation. VTT will also benchmark cost (in collaboration with UB, from task 6.4) and 
environmental footprint with simil ar linear solutions as well as measure and monitoring the transition of the A2C 
cluster towards circularity.  
VTT will participate actively in Task 7.2 defining the evaluation framework, in Task 7.5 (multidimensional analyses 
of sustainability) as well as on the validation and (T7.6) and supporting replication partners on T7.7. 
VTT applies its knowledge and experience from the different life cycle based sustainability assessment methods, and 
the experience gained over 20 years when conducting LCA projects together with different companies. Experiences 
from coordinating the SAMT project (focusing on sustainability assessment methods and tools for the process 
industry, SPIRE 2015-2016), the knowledge gained from LCA-related standardization and PEF pilot studies provide 
a solid background for the work. 
INTEREST IN THE PROJECT 
VTT has a research node of 14 scientists specialized in sustainability assessment, life cycle based assessment methods 
and circular economy. Researchers in the field of sustainability assessment are experts in LCA and evaluating 
sustainability of products, technologies and processes within various industrial sectors. VTT’s researchers have 
actively taken part in international projects (FP6, FP7 ; Horizon 2020). VTT has also participated in international 
method development such as ISO -standardization in the fields of LCA (ISO14040 -14044), carbon footprint of 
products and organisations (ISO14067, ISO 14069), water footprint (ISO14046), eco -efficiency (ISO 14045) and 
social responsibility (ISO 26000). VTT has developed and maintains a commercially available SULCA software for 
LCA, carbon and water footprint calculations.

experience in coordinating projects using diverse methods to evaluate and communicate sustainability o f 
products or companies. She is the Head of Finnish Delegation ISO TC207, expert member of ISO standards ISO 
14040 and 14044 (LCA), ISO 26000 (Social Responsibility) and ISO 14067 and 14069 (Carbon Footprint). 
Coordinator of the SAMT project (2015 -2016) in  H2020 program, WP leader in several EU -projects, e.g.

 Ms Katri Behm, (female) M. Sc. (Tech.), Research Scientist in the

4.1.30 ICONS - FONDAZIONE ICONS  
 
PARTNER Nº: 30 (NPO) 
WEBSITE: www.icube.global 
SHORTNAME: ICONS 
LOCATION: Italy 
ROLE IN THE PROJECT: A2C OUTREACH MANAGEMENT 
 
 
DESCRIPTION OF THE LEGAL ENTITY  
 
Fondazione ICONS (ICONS) is an Italian private non-profit organization, whose mission is to improve human capital 
through knowledge sharing of European and international public -funded research achievements, transparent and 
inclusive science communication, citizens’ and stakeholders’ engagement, support to innovation for the benefit of 
society. For more than 20 years ICONS has been working in public science communication, social and business 
innovation to support researchers and projects in creating impacts on society improving awareness, engagement, 
social acceptance, uptake of research results. In 2004 ICONS launched the youris.com public science communication 

Section 4,5,6-page 63 
 
platform and acknowledged today as one of the most important on -line information centers on resear ch and 
innovation in Europe. 
ICONS partners with consortia in EU and public -funded projects and non -profit organizations (research centres, 
universities, associations, etc.) coordinating and managing communication, dissemination and exploitation and 
supporting social innovation to enhance dialogue with stakeholders and the public at large. ICONS masters: web - 
based knowledge transfer tools (in 2018 ICONS won two .eu Awards for the design and implementation of two 
H2020 projects’ websites: www.stardust-project.eu and www.fetfx.eu), dissemination materials, public 
communications formats distributed globally via online, social and TV media, participation in international events 
and networking with key European umbrella organisations. ICONS measures the impacts generated by 
communication and engagement strategies through a sound methodology based on innovative outreach and 
engagement indicators. To this end, ICONS also studies and develops social indicators to measure research impacts 
on society. As part of its expertise ICONS develops social innovation frameworks, strategies and methodologies and 
carries out social acceptance analysis in community -oriented pro jects. To complete the circular and integrated 
approach aimed at optimizing and maximising impacts, ICONS develops exploitation strategies of R&I projects’ 
results by identifying and mapping key exploitable results, defining exploitation pathways (e.g. economic, scientific, 
political, replication-related, etc.), managing IPRs, analysing the market potential, designing business models and 
business plans, producing exploitation, replication and sustainability plans, involving the enablers. 
Over the past 20 years, ICONS has successfully managed communication, dissemination and exploitation activities 
in over 50 EU-funded projects (under FP4, FP5, FP6, FP7, H2020 programmes) in different research domains: Smart 
Cities, Circular Economy, Energy Efficiency, Transp ort, Bioeconomy, Environment, Security, Health, 
Nanotechnologies, Society, ICT. ICONS is part of the consortium managing the Horizon Results Booster 
dissemination services to FP7 and H2020 projects. 
 
MAIN TASKS IN THE PROJECT 
ICONS will lead WP8 -A2C outrea ch: Communication, dissemination, exploitation, training & policy 
recommendations. ICONS will prepare the A2C Outreach strategy  (T8.1) as well as will be in charge of the 
project identitity generation, project website construction  and maintaining and the A2C social networks 
management (T8.2). ICONS will be also lead the A2C Outreach beyond regional levels (T8.4) and will be in 
charge of the elaboration of the Exploitation strategy with the collaboration of all partners (T8.7) as well as will 
participate on knowledge transfer and capacity building actions (T8.6). ICONS will also contribute actively in public 
engagement related actions (7.1) and in the validation of the multidimensional model (7.7) 
INTEREST IN THE PROJECT 
ICONS has a long track record in managing communication, dissemination and exploitation activities as well as in 
defining social innovation frameworks and social evaluation in different EU funded project, covering, among others, 
smart cities and communities, circular economy, nature based solutions, bioeconomy, climate change.

 RELEVANT PROJECTS OR ACTIVITIES 
 
 URBAN GreenUP “New Strategy for Re-Naturing Cities through Nature -Based Solutions” ( 2017 – 2022),  
H2020-SCC-02-2016. Urban GreenUP aims at obtaining a tailored methodology (1) to support the co -
development of Renaturing Urban Plans focused on climate change mitigation and adaptation and efficient water 
management, and (2) to assist in the implementation of NBS in an effective way. ICONS is leader of URBAN 
GreenUP Communication and Dissemination activities, also involved in the definition of strategies for citizen 
engagement and co-creation activities, replication and exploitation activities. Website: www.urbangreenup.eu 
 HOUSEFUL “Innovative circular solutions and services for new business opportunities in the EU housing 
sector” (2018-2022), H2020-CIRC-2017 GA 776708. The main goal of the HOUSEFUL project is to develop 
and demonstrate an innovative integrated circular service in 4 full scale residential buildings, focusing on the 
optimal management/use of water, waste, energy and material resources for all stages of the life cycle of new 
builds or refurbishment of existing buildings. The service will be driven by a simple-to-use interactive Software 
as a Service (SaaS) whereby new circular economy business opportunities will be co -created and offered for 
replication for a successful transition to a circular model. Citizens shall be able to determine the efficiency of 
water, waste, energy and material and the costs of improvements through a user-friendly interactive calculation 
tool. ICONS is leader of communication and dissemination activities. Website: www.houseful.eu/  
Section 4,5,6-page 65 
 
 POCITYF “A Positive Ener gy CITY Transformation Framework” (2019 -2023), H2020 -LC-SC3-2019-ES-
SCC. POCITYF will combine positive energy blocks with grid flexibility, e -mobility and innovative ICT 
technologies and citizen engagement strategies. The overall aim is to help cities deliver positive energy districts 
while respecting their mixed urban settings that often include listed cultural heritage buildings. ICONS is leader 
of communication, dissemination and exploitation activities, and plays a key role in social innovation strategies 
and clustering activities with other EU-funded Smart City projects. Website: www.pocityf.eu 
 MAtchUP “MAximizing the UPscaling and replication potential of high level urban transformation strategies” 
(2017-2022), H2020-SCC-01-2017 - GA 774477. This project aims to drive the  transformation of Smart Cities 
in Europe, as part of the EU Smart Cities and Comm unities initiative. The MAtchUP project seeks to facilitate 
the urban transformation process by leveraging innovative solutions in the field of energy, mobility and ICT 
areas, with the involvement of citizens. ICONS leads Communication and Dissemination activities as well as the 
development of Exploitation strategies and plans. Moreover, ICONS contributes to the design and development 
of a social evaluation framework (leading social evaluation modelling and analysis) and to clustering activities 
with the Lighthouse Smart Cities projects cooperation network. Website: www.matchup-project.eu  
 STARDUST “Holistic and Integrated Urban Model for Smart Cities” (2017 -2022), H2020-SCC-01-2017 GA 
774094. In STARDUST, intelligent solutions for energy, mobility and ICT will be integrated in cities together 
with innovative business models, which will serve as blueprints for replication across Europe and abroad.  This 
synergy of actions will transform cities into living labs, pla tforms where citizens and community engagement 
will become the driving elements to improve not only their way of life but also their local economies. The project 
is fully aligned with the Clean Energy for All Europeans strategy and involves three lighthous e cities and four 
follower cities. ICONS leads Communication and Dissemination activities and contributes to clustering activities 
with the Lighthouse Smart Cities projects cooperation network. The STARDUST website 
(www.stardustproject.eu) developed by ICONS received the 2018 .eu Web Award  under the “Better World” 
Category.

4.1.32 INFO - INSTITUTO DE FOMENTO REGION DE MURCIA  
 
PARTNER Nº: 32 (Public institution)

SHORTNAME: INFO 
ROLE IN THE PROJECT: PARTNER 
 
DESCRIPTION OF THE LEGAL ENTITY  
Instituto de Fomento de la Región de Murcia (INFO Murcia) is the Regional Development Agency in Murcia. INFO 
Murcia is attached to the Regional Ministry of Enterprises & Industry responsible for co-ordinating most of aspects 
of regional economic development including promotion of technical and financial services to regional SMEs, (e.g. 
information services, entrepreneurship, business co -operation, export promotion, innovation schemes, cluster 
development, business facilities, RTD, etc), building soft infras tructures such as Technological or Business 
Innovation Centres and attracting investment to the region. Thus, INFO is considered to be a driving force behind 
the regional economy, promoting and supporting regional business sector through different aid mech anisms and 
technical services provided for the improvement of business competitiveness in the Murcia Region.   
INFO is considered the Innovation agency in the Murcia region. INFO encourages companies to incorporate 
innovation and R+TD based management stra tegies and get involved in technology transfer, ICTs, technology 
platforms and cooperation projects between companies, universities and research institutes. Furthermore, INFO 
fosters regional clusters as a key tool for industrial development, business coop eration and innovation. Thus, the 
regional cluster policy is axed through a regional network of 9 sectoral Technology Centres aimed to offer 
technological services to the industry.   
 
MAIN TASKS IN THE PROJECT 
 
INFO as dynamiser role of the regional econom y and responsible for business development in the Murcia will 
collaborate in T6.4 with UB in the development of CEBMs for the territorial development of A2C solution as well 
as will support CJM in exploring the public financing opportunities for the A2C cluster partner’s needs.

the plan with with Smart Specialisation Strategy RIS3Mur. (Within T7.5 scope) 
INFO will also supports CARM in assessing the public financing schemes at regional level (T.7.5.3) and in delivering

DESCRIPTION OF THE LEGAL ENTITY  
 
Ecotrace is a 4.0 engineering specialized in information systems that certify the traceability of materials in the 
environment. Our experience in process improvement and cloud programming allows us to create solutions in the 
circular economy market. We control raw materials and their quality standards. Our method is to analyze problems 
in real processes with our customer. Our multidisciplinary team proposes the simplest and most automated solution 
possible to increase the quality, profitability and efficiency of our client. It always incorporates dashboards for correct 
measurement of results and making strategics decisions. We program with cloud -web technology creating tools in 
mobility, flexible, fast and simple for the customer.

In WP6 they will implement the DIS as a digital tool with access to the public (T6.1). Moreover, they will be involved 
in WP8 in communication & dissemination activities (T8.2, 8.4, 8.5, 8.6,8.7). 
 
 
 
 
Related experience : They have demonstrated experience in traceability of wastes by the introduction of the
